<h1>Release 2.14.0</h1>
<p><INSERT SMALL BLURB ABOUT RELEASE FOCUS AREA AND POTENTIAL TOOLCHAIN CHANGES></p>
<h1>Breaking Changes</h1>
<ul>
<li><DOCUMENT BREAKING CHANGES HERE></li>
<li>
<p><THIS SECTION SHOULD CONTAIN API, ABI AND BEHAVIORAL BREAKING CHANGES></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.Tensor</code></p>
<ul>
<li>The class hierarchy for <code>tf.Tensor</code> has changed, and there are now
  explicit <code>EagerTensor</code> and <code>SymbolicTensor</code> classes for eager and
  tf.function respectively. Users who relied on the exact type of Tensor
  (e.g. <code>type(t) == tf.Tensor</code>) will need to update their code to use
  <code>isinstance(t, tf.Tensor)</code>. The <code>tf.is_symbolic_tensor</code> helper added in
  2.13 may be used when it is necessary to determine if a value is
  specifically a symbolic tensor.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.compat.v1.Session</code></p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.compat.v1.Session.partial_run</code> and
  <code>tf.compat.v1.Session.partial_run_setup</code> will be deprecated in the
  next release.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h1>Known Caveats</h1>
<ul>
<li><CAVEATS REGARDING THE RELEASE (BUT NOT BREAKING CHANGES).></li>
<li><ADDING/BUMPING DEPENDENCIES SHOULD GO HERE></li>
<li><KNOWN LACK OF SUPPORT ON SOME PLATFORM, SHOULD GO HERE></li>
</ul>
<h1>Major Features and Improvements</h1>
<ul>
<li><INSERT MAJOR FEATURE HERE, USING MARKDOWN SYNTAX></li>
<li><IF RELEASE CONTAINS MULTIPLE FEATURES FROM SAME AREA, GROUP THEM TOGETHER></li>
<li><code>tf.keras</code><ul>
<li><code>Model.compile</code> now support <code>steps_per_execution='auto'</code> as a parameter,
allowing automatic tuning of steps per execution during <code>Model.fit</code>,
<code>Model.predict</code>, and <code>Model.evaluate</code> for a significant performance boost. </li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h1>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h1>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.lite</code><ul>
<li>Strided_Slice now supports <code>UINT32</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><SIMILAR TO ABOVE SECTION, BUT FOR OTHER IMPORTANT CHANGES / BUG FIXES></li>
<li><IF A CHANGE CLOSES A GITHUB ISSUE, IT SHOULD BE DOCUMENTED HERE></li>
<li>
<p><NOTES SHOULD BE GROUPED PER AREA></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.config.experimental.enable_tensor_float_32_execution</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Disabling TensorFloat-32 execution now causes TPUs to use float32
  precision for float32 matmuls and other ops. TPUs have always used
  bfloat16 precision for certain ops, like matmul, when such ops had float32
  inputs. Now, disabling TensorFloat-32 by calling
  <code>tf.config.experimental.enable_tensor_float_32_execution(False)</code> will
  cause TPUs to use float32 precision for such ops instead of bfloat16.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.dtensor</code></p>
<ul>
<li>API changes for Relayout. Added a new API, <code>dtensor.relayout_like</code>, for 
  relayouting a tensor according to the layout of another tensor. </li>
<li>Added <code>dtensor.get_default_mesh</code>, for retrieving the current default 
  mesh under the dtensor context.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>TensorFlow Debugger (tfdbg) CLI: ncurses-based CLI for tfdbg v1 was removed.</p>
</li>
</ul>

<h1>Release 2.13.0</h1>
<h2>Breaking Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li><DOCUMENT BREAKING CHANGES HERE></li>
<li>
<p><THIS SECTION SHOULD CONTAIN API, ABI AND BEHAVIORAL BREAKING CHANGES></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Removed the Keras scikit-learn API wrappers (<code>KerasClassifier</code> and
   <code>KerasRegressor</code>), which had been deprecated in August 2021.
   We recommend using <a href="https://github.com/adriangb/scikeras">SciKeras</a>
   instead.</li>
<li>The default Keras model saving format is now the Keras v3 format:
   calling <code>model.save("xyz.keras")</code> will no longer create a H5 file,
   it will create a native Keras model file.
   This will only be breaking for you if you were manually inspecting or
   modifying H5 files saved by Keras under a <code>.keras</code> extension.
   If this breaks you, simply add <code>save_format="h5"</code> to your <code>.save()</code> call
   to revert back to the prior behavior.</li>
<li>Added <code>keras.utils.TimedThread</code> utility to run a timed thread every x
   seconds. It can be used to run a threaded function alongside model
   training or any other snippet of code.</li>
<li>In the <code>keras</code> PyPI package, accessible symbols are now restricted to
   symbols that are intended to be public.
   This may affect your code if you were using <code>import keras</code> and you used
   <code>keras</code> functions that were not public APIs, but were accessible in
   earlier versions with direct imports. In those cases, please use the
   following guideline:<ul>
<li>The API may be available in the public Keras API under a different
   name, so make sure to look for it on keras.io or TensorFlow docs
   and switch to the public version.</li>
<li>It could also be a simple python or TF utility that you could easily
   copy over to your own codebase. In those case, just make it your own!</li>
<li>If you believe it should definitely be a public Keras API,
   please open a feature request in keras GitHub repo.</li>
<li>As a workaround, you could import the same private symbol keras
   <code>keras.src</code>, but keep in mind the <code>src</code> namespace is not stable and
   those APIs may change or be removed in the future.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>The LMDB kernels have been changed to return an error. This is in preparation
  for completely removing them from TensorFlow. The LMDB dependency that these
  kernels are bringing to TensorFlow has been dropped, thus making the build
  slightly faster and more secure.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Known Caveats</h2>
<ul>
<li><CAVEATS REGARDING THE RELEASE (BUT NOT BREAKING CHANGES).></li>
<li><ADDING/BUMPING DEPENDENCIES SHOULD GO HERE></li>
<li><KNOWN LACK OF SUPPORT ON SOME PLATFORM, SHOULD GO HERE></li>
</ul>
<h2>Major Features and Improvements</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Add 16-bit and 64-bit float type support for built-in op <code>cast</code>.</li>
<li>The Python TF Lite Interpreter bindings now have an option
    <code>experimental_disable_delegate_clustering</code> to turn-off delegate
    clustering.</li>
<li>Add int16x8 support for the built-in op <code>exp</code></li>
<li>Add int16x8 support for the built-in op <code>mirror_pad</code></li>
<li>Add int16x8 support for the built-in ops <code>space_to_batch_nd</code> and
    <code>batch_to_space_nd</code></li>
<li>Add 16-bit int type support for built-in op <code>less</code>, <code>greater_than</code>,
    <code>equal</code></li>
<li>Add 8-bit and 16-bit support for <code>floor_div</code> and <code>floor_mod</code>.</li>
<li>Add 16-bit and 32-bit int support for the built-in op <code>bitcast</code>.</li>
<li>Add 8-bit/16-bit/32-bit int/uint support for the built-in op <code>bitwise_xor</code></li>
<li>Add int16 indices support for built-in op <code>gather</code> and <code>gather_nd</code>.</li>
<li>Add 8-bit/16-bit/32-bit int/uint support for the built-in op <code>right_shift</code></li>
<li>Add reference implementation for 16-bit int unquantized <code>add</code>.</li>
<li>Add reference implementation for 16-bit int and 32-bit unsigned int unquantized <code>mul</code>.</li>
<li><code>add_op</code> supports broadcasting up to 6 dimensions.</li>
<li>Add 16-bit support for <code>top_k</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Added F-Score metrics <code>tf.keras.metrics.FBetaScore</code>,
    <code>tf.keras.metrics.F1Score</code>, and <code>tf.keras.metrics.R2Score</code>.</li>
<li>Added activation function <code>tf.keras.activations.mish</code>.</li>
<li>Added experimental <code>keras.metrics.experimental.PyMetric</code> API for metrics
    that run Python code on the host CPU (compiled outside of the TensorFlow
    graph). This can be used for integrating metrics from external Python
    libraries (like sklearn or pycocotools) into Keras as first-class Keras
    metrics.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.optimizers.Lion</code> optimizer.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.layers.SpectralNormalization</code> layer wrapper to perform
    spectral normalization on the weights of a target layer.</li>
<li>The <code>SidecarEvaluatorModelExport</code> callback has been added to Keras as
    <code>keras.callbacks.SidecarEvaluatorModelExport</code>. This callback allows for
    exporting the model the best-scoring model as evaluated by a
    <code>SidecarEvaluator</code> evaluator. The evaluator regularly evaluates the
    model and exports it if the user-defined comparison function determines
    that it is an improvement.</li>
<li>Added warmup capabilities to <code>tf.keras.optimizers.schedules.CosineDecay</code>
    learning rate scheduler. You can now specify an initial and target
    learning rate, and our scheduler will perform a linear interpolation
    between the two after which it will begin a decay phase.</li>
<li>Added experimental support for an exactly-once visitation guarantee for
    evaluating Keras models trained with
    <code>tf.distribute.ParameterServerStrategy</code>, via the
    <code>exact_evaluation_shards</code> argument in <code>Model.fit</code> and <code>Model.evaluate</code>.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.__internal__.KerasTensor</code>,
    <code>tf.keras.__internal__.SparseKerasTensor</code>, and
    <code>tf.keras.__internal__.RaggedKerasTensor</code> classes. You can use these
    classes to do instance type checking and type annotations for
    layer/model inputs and outputs.</li>
<li>All the <code>tf.keras.dtensor.experimental.optimizers</code> classes have been 
    merged with <code>tf.keras.optimizers</code>. You can migrate your code to use
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers</code> directly. The API namespace for
    <code>tf.keras.dtensor.experimental.optimizers</code> will be removed in future
    releases.</li>
<li>Added support for <code>class_weight</code> for 3+ dimensional targets (e.g.
    image segmentation masks) in <code>Model.fit</code>.</li>
<li>Added a new loss, <code>keras.losses.CategoricalFocalCrossentropy</code>.</li>
<li>Remove the <code>tf.keras.dtensor.experimental.layout_map_scope()</code>. You can
    user the <code>tf.keras.dtensor.experimental.LayoutMap.scope()</code> instead.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.function</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>ConcreteFunction (<code>tf.types.experimental.ConcreteFunction</code>) as generated
    through <code>get_concrete_function</code> now performs holistic input validation
    similar to calling <code>tf.function</code> directly. This can cause breakages
    where existing calls pass Tensors with the wrong shape or omit certain
    non-Tensor arguments (including default values).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.nn</code></p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.nn.embedding_lookup_sparse</code> and <code>tf.nn.safe_embedding_lookup_sparse</code>
    now support ids and weights described by <code>tf.RaggedTensor</code>s.</li>
<li>Added a new boolean argument <code>allow_fast_lookup</code> to
    <code>tf.nn.embedding_lookup_sparse</code> and
    <code>tf.nn.safe_embedding_lookup_sparse</code>, which enables a simplified and
    typically faster lookup procedure.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code></p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.data.Dataset.zip</code> now supports Python-style zipping, i.e.
    <code>Dataset.zip(a, b, c)</code>.</li>
<li><code>tf.data.Dataset.shuffle</code> now supports full shuffling. To specify that
    data should be fully shuffled, use
    <code>dataset = dataset.shuffle(dataset.cardinality())</code>. This will load the
    full dataset into memory so that it can be shuffled, so make sure to
    only use this with datasets of filenames or other small datasets.</li>
<li>Added a new <code>tf.data.experimental.pad_to_cardinality</code> transformation
    which pads a dataset with zero elements up to a specified cardinality.
    This is useful for avoiding partial batches while not dropping any data.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.math</code></p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.nn.top_k</code> now supports specifying the output index type via parameter
   <code>index_type</code>.  Supported types are <code>tf.int16</code>, <code>tf.int32</code>
   (default), and <code>tf.int64</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.SavedModel</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Introduce class method
    <code>tf.saved_model.experimental.Fingerprint.from_proto(proto)</code>, which can
    be used to construct a <code>Fingerprint</code> object directly from a protobuf.</li>
<li>Introduce member method
    <code>tf.saved_model.experimental.Fingerprint.singleprint()</code>, which provides
    a convenient way to uniquely identify a SavedModel.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li><SIMILAR TO ABOVE SECTION, BUT FOR OTHER IMPORTANT CHANGES / BUG FIXES></li>
<li><IF A CHANGE CLOSES A GITHUB ISSUE, IT SHOULD BE DOCUMENTED HERE></li>
<li>
<p><NOTES SHOULD BE GROUPED PER AREA></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.Variable</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Changed resource variables to inherit from <code>tf.compat.v2.Variable</code>
    instead of <code>tf.compat.v1.Variable</code>. Some checks for 
    <code>isinstance(v, tf.compat.v1.Variable)</code> that previously returned True
    may now return False.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.distribute</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Opened an experimental API,
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.coordinator.get_current_worker_index</code>, for
    retrieving the worker index from within a worker, when using parameter
    server training with a custom training loop.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.dtensor</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Deprecated <code>dtensor.run_on</code> in favor of <code>dtensor.default_mesh</code> to
    correctly indicate that the context does not override the mesh that the
    ops and functions will run on, it only sets a fallback default mesh.</li>
<li>List of members of dtensor.Layout and dtensor.Mesh have slightly changed
    as part of efforts to consolidate the C++ and Python source
    code with pybind11. Most notably, Layout.serialized_string is removed.</li>
<li>Minor API changes to represent Single Device Layout for non-distributed
    Tensors inside DTensor functions. Runtime support will be added soon.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.ExtensionType</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.experimental.ExtensionType</code> now supports Python <code>tuple</code> as
    the type annotation of its fields.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.nest</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Deprecated API <code>tf.nest.is_sequence</code> has now been deleted.
    Please use <code>tf.nest.is_nested</code> instead.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Add UINT32 support to tfl.pack</li>
<li>Add INT64 support to tfl.range</li>
<li>Add UINT32 support to tfl.concatenation</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<h1>Release 2.12.0</h1>
<h3>Breaking Changes</h3>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Build, Compilation and Packaging</p>
<ul>
<li>Removed redundant packages <code>tensorflow-gpu</code> and <code>tf-nightly-gpu</code>. These packages were removed and replaced with packages that direct users to switch to <code>tensorflow</code> or <code>tf-nightly</code> respectively. Since TensorFlow 2.1, the only difference between these two sets of packages was their names, so there is no loss of functionality or GPU support. See https://pypi.org/project/tensorflow-gpu for more details.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.function</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.function</code> now uses the Python inspect library directly for parsing the signature of the Python function it is decorated on. This change may break code where the function signature is malformed, but was ignored previously, such as:<ul>
<li>Using <code>functools.wraps</code> on a function with different signature</li>
<li>Using <code>functools.partial</code> with an invalid <code>tf.function</code> input</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.function</code> now enforces input parameter names to be valid Python identifiers. Incompatible names are automatically sanitized similarly to existing SavedModel signature behavior.</li>
<li>Parameterless <code>tf.function</code>s are assumed to have an empty <code>input_signature</code> instead of an undefined one even if the <code>input_signature</code> is unspecified.</li>
<li><code>tf.types.experimental.TraceType</code> now requires an additional <code>placeholder_value</code> method to be defined.</li>
<li><code>tf.function</code> now traces with placeholder values generated by TraceType instead of the value itself.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Experimental APIs <code>tf.config.experimental.enable_mlir_graph_optimization</code> and <code>tf.config.experimental.disable_mlir_graph_optimization</code> were removed.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>Major Features and Improvements</h3>
<ul>
<li>Support for Python 3.11 has been added.</li>
<li>
<p>Support for Python 3.7 has been removed. We are not releasing any more patches for Python 3.7.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Add 16-bit float type support for built-in op <code>fill</code>.</li>
<li>Transpose now supports 6D tensors.</li>
<li>Float LSTM now supports diagonal recurrent tensors: https://arxiv.org/abs/1903.08023</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.dtensor</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Coordination service now works with <code>dtensor.initialize_accelerator_system</code>, and enabled by default.</li>
<li>Add <code>tf.experimental.dtensor.is_dtensor</code> to check if a tensor is a DTensor instance.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added support for alternative checkpointing protocol which makes it possible to checkpoint the state of the input pipeline without having to store the contents of internal buffers. The new functionality can be enabled through the <code>experimental_symbolic_checkpoint</code> option of <code>tf.data.Options()</code>.</li>
<li>Added a new <code>rerandomize_each_iteration</code> argument for the <code>tf.data.Dataset.random()</code> operation, which controls whether the sequence of generated random numbers should be re-randomized every epoch or not (the default behavior). If <code>seed</code> is set and <code>rerandomize_each_iteration=True</code>, the <code>random()</code> operation will produce a different (deterministic) sequence of numbers every epoch.</li>
<li>Added a new <code>rerandomize_each_iteration</code> argument for the <code>tf.data.Dataset.sample_from_datasets()</code> operation, which controls whether the sequence of generated random numbers used for sampling should be re-randomized every epoch or not. If <code>seed</code> is set and <code>rerandomize_each_iteration=True</code>, the <code>sample_from_datasets()</code> operation will use a different (deterministic) sequence of numbers every epoch.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.test</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>tf.test.experimental.sync_devices</code>, which is useful for accurately measuring performance in benchmarks.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.dtensor</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added experimental support to ReduceScatter fuse on GPU (NCCL).</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h3>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.SavedModel</code>:<ul>
<li>Introduced new class <code>tf.saved_model.experimental.Fingerprint</code> that contains the fingerprint of the SavedModel. See the <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/pull/415">SavedModel Fingerprinting RFC</a> for details.</li>
<li>Introduced API <code>tf.saved_model.experimental.read_fingerprint(export_dir)</code> for reading the fingerprint of a SavedModel.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.random</code></li>
<li>Added non-experimental aliases for <code>tf.random.split</code> and <code>tf.random.fold_in</code>, the experimental endpoints are still available so no code changes are necessary.</li>
<li><code>tf.experimental.ExtensionType</code></li>
<li>Added function <code>experimental.extension_type.as_dict()</code>, which converts an instance of <code>tf.experimental.ExtensionType</code> to a <code>dict</code> representation.</li>
<li><code>stream_executor</code></li>
<li>Top level <code>stream_executor</code> directory has been deleted, users should use equivalent headers and targets under <code>compiler/xla/stream_executor</code>.</li>
<li><code>tf.nn</code></li>
<li>Added <code>tf.nn.experimental.general_dropout</code>, which is similar to <code>tf.random.experimental.stateless_dropout</code> but accepts a custom sampler function.</li>
<li><code>tf.types.experimental.GenericFunction</code></li>
<li>The <code>experimental_get_compiler_ir</code> method supports tf.TensorSpec compilation arguments.</li>
<li><code>tf.config.experimental.mlir_bridge_rollout</code><ul>
<li>Removed enums <code>MLIR_BRIDGE_ROLLOUT_SAFE_MODE_ENABLED</code> and <code>MLIR_BRIDGE_ROLLOUT_SAFE_MODE_FALLBACK_ENABLED</code> which are no longer used by the tf2xla bridge</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Keras</h2>
<p>Keras is a framework built on top of the TensorFlow. See more details on the Keras <a href="https://keras.io/">website</a>.</p>
<h3>Breaking Changes</h3>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Moved all saving-related utilities to a new namespace, <code>keras.saving</code>, for example: <code>keras.saving.load_model</code>, <code>keras.saving.save_model</code>, <code>keras.saving.custom_object_scope</code>, <code>keras.saving.get_custom_objects</code>, <code>keras.saving.register_keras_serializable</code>,<code>keras.saving.get_registered_name</code> and <code>keras.saving.get_registered_object</code>. The previous API locations (in <code>keras.utils</code> and <code>keras.models</code>) will be available indefinitely, but we recommend you update your code to point to the new API locations.</li>
<li>Improvements and fixes in Keras loss masking:<ul>
<li>Whether you represent a ragged tensor as a <code>tf.RaggedTensor</code> or using <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/guide/keras/masking_and_padding">keras masking</a>, the returned loss values should be the identical to each other. In previous versions Keras may have silently ignored the mask.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>If you use masked losses with Keras the loss values may be different in TensorFlow <code>2.12</code> compared to previous versions.</li>
<li>In cases where the mask was previously ignored, you will now get an error if you pass a mask with an incompatible shape.</li>
</ul>
<h3>Major Features and Improvements</h3>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>The new Keras model saving format (<code>.keras</code>) is available. You can start using it via <code>model.save(f"{fname}.keras", save_format="keras_v3")</code>. In the future it will become the default for all files with the <code>.keras</code> extension. This file format targets the Python runtime only and makes it possible to reload Python objects identical to the saved originals. The format supports non-numerical state such as vocabulary files and lookup tables, and it is easy to customize in the case of custom layers with exotic elements of state (e.g. a FIFOQueue). The format does not rely on bytecode or pickling, and is safe by default. Note that as a result, Python <code>lambdas</code> are disallowed at loading time. If you want to use <code>lambdas</code>, you can pass <code>safe_mode=False</code> to the loading method (only do this if you trust the source of the model).</li>
<li>Added a <code>model.export(filepath)</code> API to create a lightweight SavedModel artifact that can be used for inference (e.g. with TF-Serving).</li>
<li>Added <code>keras.export.ExportArchive</code> class for low-level customization of the process of exporting SavedModel artifacts for inference. Both ways of exporting models are based on <code>tf.function</code> tracing and produce a TF program composed of TF ops. They are meant primarily for environments where the TF runtime is available, but not the Python interpreter, as is typical for production with TF Serving.</li>
<li>Added utility <code>tf.keras.utils.FeatureSpace</code>, a one-stop shop for structured data preprocessing and encoding.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.SparseTensor</code> input support to <code>tf.keras.layers.Embedding</code> layer. The layer now accepts a new boolean argument <code>sparse</code>. If <code>sparse</code> is set to True, the layer returns a SparseTensor instead of a dense Tensor. Defaults to False.</li>
<li>Added <code>jit_compile</code> as a settable property to <code>tf.keras.Model</code>.</li>
<li>Added <code>synchronized</code> optional parameter to <code>layers.BatchNormalization</code>.</li>
<li>Added deprecation warning to <code>layers.experimental.SyncBatchNormalization</code> and suggested to use <code>layers.BatchNormalization</code> with <code>synchronized=True</code> instead.</li>
<li>Updated <code>tf.keras.layers.BatchNormalization</code> to support masking of the inputs (<code>mask</code> argument) when computing the mean and variance.</li>
<li>Add <code>tf.keras.layers.Identity</code>, a placeholder pass-through layer.</li>
<li>Add <code>show_trainable</code> option to <code>tf.keras.utils.model_to_dot</code> to display layer trainable status in model plots.</li>
<li>Add ability to save a <code>tf.keras.utils.FeatureSpace</code> object, via <code>feature_space.save("myfeaturespace.keras")</code>, and reload it via <code>feature_space = tf.keras.models.load_model("myfeaturespace.keras")</code>.</li>
<li>Added utility <code>tf.keras.utils.to_ordinal</code> to convert class vector to ordinal regression / classification matrix.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>N/A</li>
</ul>

<h1>Release 2.11.1</h1>
<p><strong>Note</strong>: TensorFlow 2.10 was the last TensorFlow release that supported GPU on native-Windows. Starting with TensorFlow 2.11, you will need to install TensorFlow in WSL2, or install tensorflow-cpu and, optionally, try the TensorFlow-DirectML-Plugin.
*   Security vulnerability fixes will no longer be patched to this Tensorflow version. The latest Tensorflow version includes the security vulnerability fixes. You can update to the latest version (recommended) or patch security vulnerabilities yourself <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow#patching-guidelines">steps</a>. You can refer to the <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/releases">release notes</a> of the latest Tensorflow version for a list of newly fixed vulnerabilities. If you have any questions, please create a GitHub issue to let us know.</p>

<h1>Release 2.11.0</h1>
<h2>Breaking Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras.optimizers.Optimizer</code> now points to the new Keras optimizer, and
    old optimizers have moved to the <code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy</code> namespace.
    If you find your workflow failing due to this change,
    you may be facing one of the following issues:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Checkpoint loading failure.</strong> The new optimizer handles optimizer
    state differently from the old optimizer, which simplies the logic of
    checkpoint saving/loading, but at the cost of breaking checkpoint
    backward compatibility in some cases. If you want to keep using an old
    checkpoint, please change your optimizer to
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy.XXX</code> (e.g.
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy.Adam</code>).</li>
<li><strong>TF1 compatibility.</strong> The new optimizer does not support TF1 any more,
    so please use the legacy optimizer <code>tf.keras.optimizer.legacy.XXX</code>.
    We highly recommend to migrate your workflow to TF2 for stable
    support and new features.</li>
<li><strong>API not found.</strong> The new optimizer has a different set of public APIs
    from the old optimizer. These API changes are mostly related to
    getting rid of slot variables and TF1 support. Please check the API
    documentation to find alternatives to the missing API. If you must
    call the deprecated API, please change your optimizer to the legacy
    optimizer.</li>
<li><strong>Learning rate schedule access.</strong> When using a <code>LearningRateSchedule</code>,
    The new optimizer's <code>learning_rate</code> property returns the
    current learning rate value instead of a <code>LearningRateSchedule</code> object
    as before. If you need to access the <code>LearningRateSchedule</code> object,
    please use <code>optimizer._learning_rate</code>.</li>
<li><strong>You implemented a custom optimizer based on the old optimizer.</strong>
    Please set your optimizer to subclass
    <code>tf.keras.optimizer.legacy.XXX</code>. If you want to migrate to the new
    optimizer and find it does not support your optimizer, please file
    an issue in the Keras GitHub repo.</li>
<li><strong>Error such as <code>Cannot recognize variable...</code>.</strong> The new optimizer
    requires all optimizer variables to be created at the first
    <code>apply_gradients()</code> or <code>minimize()</code> call. If your workflow calls
    optimizer to update different parts of model in multiple stages,
    please call <code>optimizer.build(model.trainable_variables)</code> before the
    training loop.</li>
<li><strong>Performance regression on <code>ParameterServerStrategy</code>.</strong> This could be
    significant if you have many PS servers. We are aware of this issue and
    working on fixes, for now we suggest using the legacy optimizers when
    using <code>ParameterServerStrategy</code>.</li>
<li><strong>Timeout or performance loss.</strong> We don't anticipate this to happen, but
    if you see such issues, please use the legacy optimizer, and file
    an issue in the Keras GitHub repo.</li>
</ul>
<p>The old Keras optimizer will never be deleted, but will not see any
new feature additions.
New optimizers (e.g., <code>Adafactor</code>) will
only be implemented based on <code>tf.keras.optimizers.Optimizer</code>, the new
base class.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Major Features and Improvements</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>New operations supported:<ul>
<li>tf.unsortedsegmentmin op is supported.</li>
<li>tf.atan2 op is supported.</li>
<li>tf.sign op is supported.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Updates to existing operations:<ul>
<li>tfl.mul now supports complex32 inputs.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.StructuredTensor</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Introduced <code>tf.experimental.StructuredTensor</code>, which provides a flexible
    and Tensorflow-native way to encode structured data such as protocol
    buffers or pandas dataframes.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added method <code>get_metrics_result()</code> to <code>tf.keras.models.Model</code>.<ul>
<li>Returns the current metrics values of the model as a dict.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Added group normalization layer <code>tf.keras.layers.GroupNormalization</code>.</li>
<li>Added weight decay support for all Keras optimizers.</li>
<li>Added Adafactor optimizer <code>tf.keras.optimizers.Adafactor</code>.</li>
<li>Added <code>warmstart_embedding_matrix</code> to <code>tf.keras.utils</code>.
    This utility can be used to warmstart an embeddings matrix so you
    reuse previously-learned word embeddings when working with a new set
    of words which may include previously unseen words (the embedding
    vectors for unseen words will be randomly initialized).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.Variable</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>CompositeTensor</code> as a baseclass to <code>ResourceVariable</code>. This
    allows <code>tf.Variable</code>s to be nested in <code>tf.experimental.ExtensionType</code>s.</li>
<li>Added a new constructor argument <code>experimental_enable_variable_lifting</code>
    to <code>tf.Variable</code>, defaulting to True. When it's <code>False</code>, the variable
    won't be lifted out of <code>tf.function</code>, thus it can be used as a
    <code>tf.function</code>-local variable: during each execution of the
    <code>tf.function</code>, the variable will be created and then disposed, similar
    to a local (i.e. stack-allocated) variable in C/C++. Currently
    <code>experimental_enable_variable_lifting=False</code> only works on non-XLA
    devices (e.g. under <code>@tf.function(jit_compile=False)</code>).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>TF SavedModel:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>fingerprint.pb</code> to the SavedModel directory. The <code>fingerprint.pb</code>
    file is a protobuf containing the "fingerprint" of the SavedModel. See
    the <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/pull/415">RFC</a> for more
    details regarding its design and properties.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Graduated experimental APIs:<ul>
<li><a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/Dataset/#ragged_batch"><code>tf.data.Dataset.ragged_batch</code></a>, which batches elements of <code>tf.data.Dataset</code>s into <code>tf.RaggedTensor</code>s.</li>
<li><a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/Dataset/#sparse_batch"><code>tf.data.Dataset.sparse_batch</code></a>, which batches elements of <code>tf.data.Dataset</code>s into <code>tf.sparse.SparseTensor</code>s.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.image</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Added an optional parameter <code>return_index_map</code> to <code>tf.image.ssim</code> which
    causes the returned value to be the local SSIM map instead of the global
    mean.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>TF Core:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.custom_gradient</code> can now be applied to functions that accept
    "composite" tensors, such as <code>tf.RaggedTensor</code>, as inputs.</li>
<li>Fix device placement issues related to datasets with ragged tensors of
    strings (i.e. variant encoded data with types not supported on GPU).</li>
<li>'experimental_follow_type_hints' for tf.function has been deprecated.
    Please use input_signature or reduce_retracing to minimize retracing.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.SparseTensor</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Introduced <code>set_shape</code>, which sets the static dense shape of the sparse tensor and has the same semantics as <code>tf.Tensor.set_shape</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Security</h2>
<ul>
<li>TF is currently using giflib 5.2.1 which has <a href="https://nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2022-28506">CVE-2022-28506</a>. TF is not affected by the CVE as it does not use <code>DumpScreen2RGB</code> at all.</li>
<li>Fixes an OOB seg fault in <code>DynamicStitch</code> due to missing validation (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41883">CVE-2022-41883</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an overflow in <code>tf.keras.losses.poisson</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41887">CVE-2022-41887</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap OOB failure in <code>ThreadUnsafeUnigramCandidateSampler</code> caused by missing validation (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41880">CVE-2022-41880</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>ndarray_tensor_bridge</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41884">CVE-2022-41884</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an overflow in <code>FusedResizeAndPadConv2D</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41885">CVE-2022-41885</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a overflow in <code>ImageProjectiveTransformV2</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41886">CVE-2022-41886</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an FPE in <code>tf.image.generate_bounding_box_proposals</code> on GPU (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41888">CVE-2022-41888</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>pywrap_tfe_src</code> caused by invalid attributes (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41889">CVE-2022-41889</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code> fail in <code>BCast</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41890">CVE-2022-41890</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>TensorListConcat</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41891">CVE-2022-41891</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK_EQ</code> fail in <code>TensorListResize</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41893">CVE-2022-41893</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an overflow in <code>CONV_3D_TRANSPOSE</code> on TFLite (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41894">CVE-2022-41894</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap OOB in <code>MirrorPadGrad</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41895">CVE-2022-41895</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a crash in <code>Mfcc</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41896">CVE-2022-41896</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap OOB in <code>FractionalMaxPoolGrad</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41897">CVE-2022-41897</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code> fail in <code>SparseFillEmptyRowsGrad</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-41898">CVE-2022-41898</a>)</li>

<h1>Release 2.10.0</h1>
<h2>Breaking Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>Causal attention in <code>keras.layers.Attention</code> and
    <code>keras.layers.AdditiveAttention</code> is now specified in the <code>call()</code> method via
    the <code>use_causal_mask</code> argument (rather than in the constructor), for
    consistency with other layers.</li>
<li>Some files in <code>tensorflow/python/training</code> have been moved to
    <code>tensorflow/python/tracking</code> and <code>tensorflow/python/checkpoint</code>. Please
    update your imports accordingly, the old files will be removed in Release
    2.11.</li>
<li><code>tf.keras.optimizers.experimental.Optimizer</code> will graduate in Release 2.11,
    which means <code>tf.keras.optimizers.Optimizer</code> will be an alias of
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.experimental.Optimizer</code>. The current
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.Optimizer</code> will continue to be supported as
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy.Optimizer</code>,
    e.g.,<code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy.Adam</code>. Most users won't be affected by this
    change, but please check the
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/optimizers/experimental">API doc</a>
    if any API used in your workflow is changed or deprecated, and make
    adaptations. If you decide to keep using the old optimizer, please
    explicitly change your optimizer to <code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy.Optimizer</code>.</li>
<li>RNG behavior change for <code>tf.keras.initializers</code>. Keras initializers will now
    use stateless random ops to generate random numbers.<ul>
<li>Both seeded and unseeded initializers will always generate the same
    values every time they are called (for a given variable shape). For
    unseeded initializers (<code>seed=None</code>), a random seed will be created and
    assigned at initializer creation (different initializer instances get
    different seeds).</li>
<li>An unseeded initializer will raise a warning if it is reused (called)
    multiple times. This is because it would produce the same values each
    time, which may not be intended.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>API changes under <code>tf.experimental.dtensor</code>:<ul>
<li>New API for initialization of CPU/GPU/TPU in dtensor.
    <code>dtensor.initialize_accelerator_system</code> and
    <code>dtensor.shutdown_accelerator_system</code>.</li>
<li>The following existing API will be removed:
    <code>dtensor.initialize_multi_client</code>, <code>dtensor.initialize_tpu_system</code>, and
    <code>dtensor.shutdown_tpu_system</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Deprecations</h2>
<ul>
<li>The C++ <code>tensorflow::Code</code> and <code>tensorflow::Status</code> will become aliases of
    respectively <code>absl::StatusCode</code> and <code>absl::Status</code> in some future release.<ul>
<li>Use <code>tensorflow::OkStatus()</code> instead of <code>tensorflow::Status::OK()</code>.</li>
<li>Stop constructing <code>Status</code> objects from <code>tensorflow::error::Code</code>.</li>
<li>One MUST NOT access <code>tensorflow::errors::Code</code> fields. Accessing
    <code>tensorflow::error::Code</code> fields is fine.<ul>
<li>Use the constructors such as <code>tensorflow::errors:InvalidArgument</code> to
    create status using an error code without accessing it.</li>
<li>Use the free functions such as
    <code>tensorflow::errors::IsInvalidArgument</code> if needed.</li>
<li>In the last resort, use
    e.g.<code>static_cast&lt;tensorflow::errors::Code&gt;(error::Code::INVALID_ARGUMENT)</code>
    or <code>static_cast&lt;int&gt;(code)</code> for comparisons.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tensorflow::StatusOr</code> will also become in the future an alias to
    <code>absl::StatusOr</code>, so use <code>StatusOr::value</code> instead of
    <code>StatusOr::ConsumeValueOrDie</code>.</li>
</ul>
<h2>Major Features and Improvements</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>New operations supported:<ul>
<li>tflite SelectV2 now supports 5D.</li>
<li><code>tf.einsum</code> is supported with multiple unknown shapes.</li>
<li><code>tf.unsortedsegmentprod</code> op is supported.</li>
<li><code>tf.unsortedsegmentmax</code> op is supported.</li>
<li><code>tf.unsortedsegmentsum</code> op is supported.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Updates to existing operations:<ul>
<li><code>tfl.scatter_nd</code> now supports I1 for the <code>update</code> arg.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Upgrade Flatbuffers v2.0.5 from v1.12.0</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>EinsumDense</code> layer is moved from experimental to core. Its import path
    is moved from <code>tf.keras.layers.experimental.EinsumDense</code> to
    <code>tf.keras.layers.EinsumDense</code>.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.utils.audio_dataset_from_directory</code> utility to easily
    generate audio classification datasets from directories of <code>.wav</code> files.</li>
<li>Added <code>subset="both"</code> support in
    <code>tf.keras.utils.image_dataset_from_directory</code>,<code>tf.keras.utils.text_dataset_from_directory</code>,
    and <code>audio_dataset_from_directory</code>, to be used with the
    <code>validation_split</code> argument, for returning both dataset splits at once,
    as a tuple.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.utils.split_dataset</code> utility to split a <code>Dataset</code> object
    or a list/tuple of arrays into two <code>Dataset</code> objects (e.g. train/test).</li>
<li>Added step granularity to <code>BackupAndRestore</code> callback for handling
    distributed training failures &amp; restarts. The training state can now be
    restored at the exact epoch and step at which it was previously saved
    before failing.</li>
<li>Added
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/dtensor/experimental/optimizers/AdamW"><code>tf.keras.dtensor.experimental.optimizers.AdamW</code></a>.
    This optimizer is similar to the existing
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/optimizers/experimental/AdamW"><code>keras.optimizers.experimental.AdamW</code></a>,
    and works in the DTensor training use case.</li>
<li>Improved masking support for
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/layers/MultiHeadAttention"><code>tf.keras.layers.MultiHeadAttention</code></a>.<ul>
<li>Implicit masks for <code>query</code>, <code>key</code> and <code>value</code> inputs will
    automatically be used to compute a correct attention mask for the
    layer. These padding masks will be combined with any
    <code>attention_mask</code> passed in directly when calling the layer. This can
    be used with
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/layers/Embedding"><code>tf.keras.layers.Embedding</code></a>
    with <code>mask_zero=True</code> to automatically infer a correct padding mask.</li>
<li>Added a <code>use_causal_mask</code> call time argument to the layer. Passing
    <code>use_causal_mask=True</code> will compute a causal attention mask, and
    optionally combine it with any <code>attention_mask</code> passed in directly
    when calling the layer.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Added <code>ignore_class</code> argument in the loss
    <code>SparseCategoricalCrossentropy</code> and metrics <code>IoU</code> and <code>MeanIoU</code>, to
    specify a class index to be ignored during loss/metric computation (e.g.
    a background/void class).</li>
<li>Added
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/models/experimental/SharpnessAwareMinimization"><code>tf.keras.models.experimental.SharpnessAwareMinimization</code></a>.
    This class implements the sharpness-aware minimization technique, which
    boosts model performance on various tasks, e.g., ResNet on image
    classification.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added support for cross-trainer data caching in tf.data service. This
    saves computation resources when concurrent training jobs train from the
    same dataset. See
    (https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/experimental/service#sharing_tfdata_service_with_concurrent_trainers)
    for more details.</li>
<li>Added <code>dataset_id</code> to <code>tf.data.experimental.service.register_dataset</code>.
    If provided, <code>tf.data</code> service will use the provided ID for the dataset.
    If the dataset ID already exists, no new dataset will be registered.
    This is useful if multiple training jobs need to use the same dataset
    for training. In this case, users should call <code>register_dataset</code> with
    the same <code>dataset_id</code>.</li>
<li>Added a new field, <code>inject_prefetch</code>, to
    <code>tf.data.experimental.OptimizationOptions</code>. If it is set to
    <code>True</code>,<code>tf.data</code> will now automatically add a <code>prefetch</code> transformation
    to datasets that end in synchronous transformations. This enables data
    generation to be overlapped with data consumption. This may cause a
    small increase in memory usage due to buffering. To enable this
    behavior, set <code>inject_prefetch=True</code> in
    <code>tf.data.experimental.OptimizationOptions</code>.</li>
<li>Added a new value to <code>tf.data.Options.autotune.autotune_algorithm</code>:
    <code>STAGE_BASED</code>. If the autotune algorithm is set to <code>STAGE_BASED</code>, then
    it runs a new algorithm that can get the same performance with lower
    CPU/memory usage.</li>
<li>Added
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/experimental/from_list"><code>tf.data.experimental.from_list</code></a>,
    a new API for creating <code>Dataset</code>s from lists of elements.</li>
<li>Graduated experimental APIs:<ul>
<li><a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/Dataset/#counter"><code>tf.data.Dataset.counter</code></a>,
    which creates <code>Dataset</code>s of indefinite sequences of numbers.</li>
<li><a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/Dataset/#ignore_errors"><code>tf.data.Dataset.ignore_errors</code></a>,
    which drops erroneous elements from <code>Dataset</code>s.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Added
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/Dataset#rebatch"><code>tf.data.Dataset.rebatch</code></a>,
    a new API for rebatching the elements of a dataset.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.distribute</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/distribute/experimental/PreemptionCheckpointHandler"><code>tf.distribute.experimental.PreemptionCheckpointHandler</code></a>
    to handle worker preemption/maintenance and cluster-wise consistent
    error reporting for <code>tf.distribute.MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy</code>.
    Specifically, for the type of interruption with advance notice, it
    automatically saves a checkpoint, exits the program without raising an
    unrecoverable error, and restores the progress when training restarts.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.math</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>tf.math.approx_max_k</code> and <code>tf.math.approx_min_k</code> which are the
    optimized alternatives to <code>tf.math.top_k</code> on TPU. The performance
    difference ranges from 8 to 100 times depending on the size of k. When
    running on CPU and GPU, a non-optimized XLA kernel is used.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.train</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>tf.train.TrackableView</code> which allows users to inspect the
    TensorFlow Trackable object (e.g. <code>tf.Module</code>, Keras Layers and models).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.vectorized_map</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added an optional parameter: <code>warn</code>. This parameter controls whether or
    not warnings will be printed when operations in the provided <code>fn</code> fall
    back to a while loop.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>XLA:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.distribute.MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy</code> is now compilable with XLA.</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/ARM-software/ComputeLibrary">Compute Library for the Arm® Architecture (ACL)</a>
    is supported for aarch64 CPU XLA runtime</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>CPU performance optimizations:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>x86 CPUs</strong>:
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/blob/master/rfcs/20210930-enable-onednn-ops.md">oneDNN</a>
    bfloat16 auto-mixed precision grappler graph optimization pass has been
    renamed from <code>auto_mixed_precision_mkl</code> to
    <code>auto_mixed_precision_onednn_bfloat16</code>. See example usage
    <a href="https://www.intel.com/content/www/us/en/developer/articles/guide/getting-started-with-automixedprecisionmkl.html">here</a>.</li>
<li><strong>aarch64 CPUs:</strong> Experimental performance optimizations from
    <a href="https://github.com/ARM-software/ComputeLibrary">Compute Library for the Arm® Architecture (ACL)</a>
    are available through oneDNN in the default Linux aarch64 package (<code>pip
    install tensorflow</code>).<ul>
<li>The optimizations are disabled by default.</li>
<li>Set the environment variable <code>TF_ENABLE_ONEDNN_OPTS=1</code> to enable the
    optimizations. Setting the variable to 0 or unsetting it will
    disable the optimizations.</li>
<li>These optimizations can yield slightly different numerical results
    from when they are off due to floating-point round-off errors from
    different computation approaches and orders.</li>
<li>To verify that the optimizations are on, look for a message with
    "<em>oneDNN custom operations are on</em>" in the log. If the exact phrase
    is not there, it means they are off.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p>New argument <code>experimental_device_ordinal</code> in <code>LogicalDeviceConfiguration</code>
    to control the order of logical devices (GPU only).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Changed the TensorBoard tag names produced by the
    <code>tf.keras.callbacks.TensorBoard</code> callback, so that summaries logged
    automatically for model weights now include either a <code>/histogram</code> or
    <code>/image</code> suffix in their tag names, in order to prevent tag name
    collisions across summary types.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>When running on GPU (with cuDNN version 7.6.3 or
    later),<code>tf.nn.depthwise_conv2d</code> backprop to <code>filter</code> (and therefore also
    <code>tf.keras.layers.DepthwiseConv2D</code>) now operate deterministically (and
    <code>tf.errors.UnimplementedError</code> is no longer thrown) when op-determinism has
    been enabled via <code>tf.config.experimental.enable_op_determinism</code>. This closes
    issue <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/47174">47174</a>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.random</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>tf.random.experimental.stateless_shuffle</code>, a stateless version of
    <code>tf.random.shuffle</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

*   Fixes a <code>CHECK</code> failure in tf.reshape caused by overflows (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-35934">CVE-2022-35934</a>)

<h1>Release 2.9.1</h1>
<p>Add an upper bound for <code>protobuf</code> in <code>setup.py</code> since <code>protobuf</code> after version 3.20 is currently incompatible with TensorFlow. See https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/53234, https://github.com/protocolbuffers/protobuf/issues/9954 and https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/56077.</p>

See https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/53234, https://github.com/protocolbuffers/protobuf/issues/9954 and https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/56077.</p>

<h1>Release 2.9.0</h1>
<h2>Breaking Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>Due to security issues in TF 2.8, all boosted trees code has now been removed (after being deprecated in TF 2.8). Users should switch to <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/decision-forests">TensorFlow Decision Forests</a>.</li>
<li>Build, Compilation and Packaging<ul>
<li>TensorFlow is now compiled with <code>_GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI=1</code>. Downstream projects that encounter <code>std::__cxx11</code> or <code>[abi:cxx11]</code> linker errors will need to adopt this compiler option. See <a href="https://gcc.gnu.org/onlinedocs/libstdc++/manual/using_dual_abi.html">the GNU C++ Library docs on Dual ABI</a>.</li>
<li>TensorFlow Python wheels now specifically conform to <a href="https://peps.python.org/pep-0599/">manylinux2014</a>, an upgrade from manylinux2010. The minimum Pip version supporting manylinux2014 is Pip 19.3 (see <a href="https://github.com/pypa/manylinux">pypa/manylinux</a>. This change may affect you if you have been using TensorFlow on a very old platform equivalent to CentOS 6, as manylinux2014 targets CentOS 7 as a compatibility base. Note that TensorFlow does not officially support either platform.</li>
<li>Discussion for these changes can be found on SIG Build's <a href="https://discuss.tensorflow.org/t/tensorflow-linux-wheels-are-being-upgraded-to-manylinux2014/8339">TensorFlow Community Forum thread</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental</code> API has been removed. The non-experimental symbols under <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision</code> have been available since TensorFlow 2.4 and should be used instead.<ul>
<li>The non-experimental API has some minor differences from the experimental API. In most cases, you only need to make three minor changes:</li>
<li>Remove the word "experimental" from <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision</code> symbols. E.g., replace <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.global_policy</code> with <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.global_policy</code>.</li>
<li>Replace <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.set_policy</code> with <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.set_global_policy</code>. The experimental symbol <code>set_policy</code> was renamed to <code>set_global_policy</code> in the non-experimental API.</li>
<li>Replace <code>LossScaleOptimizer(opt, "dynamic")</code> with <code>LossScaleOptimizer(opt)</code>. If you pass anything other than <code>"dynamic"</code> to the second argument, see (1) of the next section.</li>
<li>In the following rare cases, you need to make more changes when switching to the non-experimental API:</li>
<li>If you passed anything other than <code>"dynamic"</code> to the <code>loss_scale</code> argument (the second argument) of <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code>:<ul>
<li>The LossScaleOptimizer constructor takes in different arguments. See the <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/versions/r2.7/api_docs/python/tf/keras/mixed_precision/experimental/LossScaleOptimizer">TF 2.7 documentation of tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScaleOptimizer</a> for details on the differences, which has examples on how to convert to the non-experimental LossScaleOptimizer.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>If you passed a value to the <code>loss_scale</code> argument (the second argument) of <code>Policy</code>:<ul>
<li>The experimental version of <code>Policy</code> optionally took in a <code>tf.compat.v1.mixed_precision.LossScale</code> in the constructor, which defaulted to a dynamic loss scale for the <code>"mixed_float16"</code> policy and no loss scale for other policies. In <code>Model.compile</code>, if the model's policy had a loss scale, the optimizer would be wrapped with a <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code>. With the non-experimental <code>Policy</code>, there is no loss scale associated with the <code>Policy</code>, and <code>Model.compile</code> wraps the optimizer with a <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code> if and only if the policy is a <code>"mixed_float16"</code> policy. If you previously passed a <code>LossScale</code> to the experimental <code>Policy</code>, consider just removing it, as the default loss scaling behavior is usually what you want. If you really want to customize the loss scaling behavior, you can wrap your optimizer with a <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code> before passing it to <code>Model.compile</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>If you use the very rarely-used function <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.get_layer_policy</code>:<ul>
<li>Replace <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.get_layer_policy(layer)</code> with <code>layer.dtype_policy</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScale</code> and its subclasses have been removed from the TF2 namespace. This symbols were very rarely used and were only useful in TF2 for use in the now-removed <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental</code> API. The symbols are still available under <code>tf.compat.v1.mixed_precision</code>.</li>
<li>The <code>experimental_relax_shapes</code> heuristic for <code>tf.function</code> has been deprecated and replaced with <code>reduce_retracing</code> which encompasses broader heuristics to reduce the number of retraces (see below)</li>
</ul>
<h2>Major Features and Improvements</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.applications.resnet_rs</code> models. This includes the
    <code>ResNetRS50</code>, <code>ResNetRS101</code>, <code>ResNetRS152</code>, <code>ResNetRS200</code>,
    <code>ResNetRS270</code>, <code>ResNetRS350</code> and <code>ResNetRS420</code> model architectures. The
    ResNetRS models are based on the architecture described in
    <a href="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2103.07579.pdf">Revisiting ResNets: Improved Training and Scaling Strategies</a></li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.optimizers.experimental.Optimizer</code>. The reworked
    optimizer gives more control over different phases of optimizer calls,
    and is easier to customize. We provide Adam, SGD, Adadelta, AdaGrad and
    RMSprop optimizers based on
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.experimental.Optimizer</code>. Generally the new
    optimizers work in the same way as the old ones, but support new
    constructor arguments. In the future, the symbols
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.Optimizer</code>/<code>Adam</code>/etc will point to the new
    optimizers, and the previous generation of optimizers will be moved to
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.legacy.Optimizer</code>/<code>Adam</code>/etc.</li>
<li>Added L2 unit normalization layer <code>tf.keras.layers.UnitNormalization</code>.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.regularizers.OrthogonalRegularizer</code>, a new regularizer
    that encourages orthogonality between the rows (or columns) or a weight
    matrix.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.keras.layers.RandomBrightness</code> layer for image preprocessing.</li>
<li>Added APIs for switching between interactive logging and absl logging.
    By default, Keras always writes the logs to stdout. However, this is not
    optimal in a non-interactive environment, where you don't have access to
    stdout, but can only view the logs. You can use
    <code>tf.keras.utils.disable_interactive_logging()</code> to write the logs to ABSL
    logging. You can also use <code>tf.keras.utils.enable_interactive_logging()</code>
    to change it back to stdout, or
    <code>tf.keras.utils.is_interactive_logging_enabled()</code> to check if
    interactive logging is enabled.</li>
<li>Changed default value for the <code>verbose</code> argument of <code>Model.evaluate()</code>
    and <code>Model.predict()</code> to <code>"auto"</code>, which defaults to <code>verbose=1</code> for
    most cases and defaults to <code>verbose=2</code> when used with
    <code>ParameterServerStrategy</code> or with interactive logging disabled.</li>
<li>Argument <code>jit_compile</code> in <code>Model.compile()</code> now applies to
    <code>Model.evaluate()</code> and <code>Model.predict()</code>. Setting <code>jit_compile=True</code> in
    <code>compile()</code> compiles the model's training, evaluation, and inference
    steps to <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/xla">XLA</a>. Note that
    <code>jit_compile=True</code> may not necessarily work for all models.</li>
<li>Added DTensor-related Keras APIs under <code>tf.keras.dtensor</code> namespace. The
    APIs are still classified as experimental. You are welcome to try it
    out. Please check the tutorial and guide on https://www.tensorflow.org/
    for more details about DTensor.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added TFLite builtin op support for the following TF ops:<ul>
<li><code>tf.math.argmin</code>/<code>tf.math.argmax</code> for input data type <code>tf.bool</code> on
    CPU.</li>
<li><code>tf.nn.gelu</code> op for output data type <code>tf.float32</code> and quantization
    on CPU.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Add nominal support for unsigned 16-bit integer tensor types. Note that
    very few TFLite kernels support this type natively, so its use in mobile
    ML authoring is generally discouraged.</li>
<li>Add support for unsigned 16-bit integer tensor types in cast op.</li>
<li>Experimental support for lowering <code>list_ops.tensor_list_set_item</code> with
    <code>DynamicUpdateSlice</code>.</li>
<li>Enabled a new MLIR-based dynamic range quantization backend by default<ul>
<li>The new backend is used for post-training int8 dynamic range
    quantization and post-training float16 quantization.</li>
<li>Set <code>experimental_new_dynamic_range_quantizer</code> in
    tf.lite.TFLiteConverter to False to disable this change</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Native TF Lite variables are now enabled during conversion by default on
    all v2 TfLiteConverter entry points.
    <code>experimental_enable_resource_variables</code> on tf.lite.TFLiteConverter is
    now True by default and will be removed in the future.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.function</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Custom classes used as arguments for <code>tf.function</code> can now specify rules
    regarding when retracing needs to occur by implementing the Tracing
    Protocol available through
    <code>tf.types.experimental.SupportsTracingProtocol</code>.</li>
<li><code>TypeSpec</code> classes (as associated with <code>ExtensionTypes</code>) also implement
    the Tracing Protocol which can be overridden if necessary.</li>
<li>The newly introduced <code>reduce_retracing</code> option also uses the Tracing
    Protocol to proactively generate generalized traces similar to
    <code>experimental_relax_shapes</code> (which has now been deprecated).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unified eager and <code>tf.function</code> execution:</p>
<ul>
<li>Eager mode can now execute each op as a <code>tf.function</code>, allowing for more
    consistent feature support in future releases.</li>
<li>It is available for immediate use.<ul>
<li>See the <code>TF_RUN_EAGER_OP_AS_FUNCTION</code> environment variable in
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/blob/master/tensorflow/python/eager/context.py">eager context</a>.</li>
<li>Eager performance should be similar with this feature enabled.<ul>
<li>A roughly 5us per-op overhead may be observed when running many
    small functions.</li>
<li>Note a
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/55414">known issue</a>
    with GPU performance.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The behavior of <code>tf.function</code> itself is unaffected.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Note: This feature will be enabled by default in an upcoming version of
    TensorFlow.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.experimental.dtensor</code>: Added DTensor, an extension to TensorFlow for
    large-scale modeling with minimal changes to user code. You are welcome to
    try it out, though be aware that the DTensor API is experimental and up-to
    backward-incompatible changes. DTensor and Keras integration is published
    under <code>tf.keras.dtensor</code> in this release (refer to the <code>tf.keras</code> entry).
    The tutoral and guide for DTensor will be published on
    https://www.tensorflow.org/. Please stay tuned.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/blob/master/rfcs/20210930-enable-onednn-ops.md">oneDNN CPU performance optimizations</a>
    are available in Linux x86, Windows x86, and Linux aarch64 packages.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Linux x86 packages:</strong><ul>
<li>oneDNN optimizations are <em>enabled by default</em> on CPUs with
    neural-network-focused hardware features such as AVX512_VNNI,
    AVX512_BF16, AMX, etc.
    (<a href="https://www.intel.com/content/www/us/en/products/platforms/details/cascade-lake.html">Intel Cascade Lake</a>
    and newer CPUs.)<ul>
<li><a href="https://medium.com/intel-analytics-software/leverage-intel-deep-learning-optimizations-in-tensorflow-129faa80ee07">Example performance speedups.</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>For older CPUs, oneDNN optimizations are disabled by default.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Windows x86 package:</strong> oneDNN optimizations are disabled by default.</li>
<li><strong>Linux aach64 (<code>--config=mkl_aarch64</code>) package:</strong><ul>
<li>Experimental oneDNN optimizations are disabled by default.</li>
<li>If you experience issues with oneDNN optimizations on, we recommend
    turning them off.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>To explicitly enable or disable oneDNN optimizations, set the
    environment variable <code>TF_ENABLE_ONEDNN_OPTS</code> to <code>1</code> (enable) or <code>0</code>
    (disable) before running TensorFlow. (The variable is checked during
    <code>import tensorflow</code>.) To fall back to default settings, unset the
    environment variable.</li>
<li>These optimizations can yield slightly different numerical results from
    when they are off due to floating-point round-off errors from different
    computation approaches and orders.</li>
<li>To verify that the optimizations are on, look for a message with
    <em>"oneDNN custom operations are on"</em> in the log. If the exact phrase is
    not there, it means they are off.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fixed bug in <code>tf.data.experimental.parse_example_dataset</code> when <code>tf.io.RaggedFeatures</code> would specify <code>value_key</code> but no <code>partitions</code>. Before the fix, setting <code>value_key</code> but no <code>partitions</code> would result in the feature key being replaced by the value key, e.g. <code>{'value_key': &lt;RaggedTensor&gt;}</code> instead of <code>{'key': &lt;RaggedTensor&gt;}</code>. Now the correct feature key will be used. This aligns the behavior of <code>tf.data.experimental.parse_example_dataset</code> to match the behavior of <code>tf.io.parse_example</code>.</li>
<li>Added a new field, <code>filter_parallelization</code>, to <code>tf.data.experimental.OptimizationOptions</code>. If it is set to <code>True</code>, tf.data will run <code>Filter</code> transformation with multiple threads. Its default value is <code>False</code> if not specified.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fixed bug in optimizers that prevented them from properly checkpointing slot variables when they are <code>ShardedVariable</code>s (used for training with <code>tf.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code>).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.random</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Added <code>tf.random.experimental.index_shuffle</code>, for shuffling a sequence without materializing the sequence in memory.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.RaggedTensor</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Introduced <code>tf.experimental.RowPartition</code>, which encodes how one dimension in a RaggedTensor relates to another, into the public API.</li>
<li>Introduced <code>tf.experimental.DynamicRaggedShape</code>, which represents the shape of a RaggedTensor.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Security</h2>
<ul>
<li>Fixes a code injection in <code>saved_model_cli</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29216">CVE-2022-29216</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes <code>TensorSummaryV2</code> to crash (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29193">CVE-2022-29193</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which crashes <code>QuantizeAndDequantizeV4Grad</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29192">CVE-2022-29192</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>DeleteSessionTensor</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29194">CVE-2022-29194</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>GetSessionTensor</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29191">CVE-2022-29191</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>StagePeek</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29195">CVE-2022-29195</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>UnsortedSegmentJoin</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29197">CVE-2022-29197</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>LoadAndRemapMatrix</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29199">CVE-2022-29199</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>SparseTensorToCSRSparseMatrix</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29198">CVE-2022-29198</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>LSTMBlockCell</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29200">CVE-2022-29200</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>Conv3DBackpropFilterV2</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29196">CVE-2022-29196</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code> failure in depthwise ops via overflows (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-41197">CVE-2021-41197</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes issues arising from undefined behavior stemming from users supplying invalid resource handles (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29207">CVE-2022-29207</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault due to missing support for quantized types (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29205">CVE-2022-29205</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which results in undefined behavior in <code>SparseTensorDenseAdd</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29206">CVE-2022-29206</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which results in undefined behavior in <code>QuantizedConv2D</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29201">CVE-2022-29201</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an integer overflow in <code>SpaceToBatchND</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29203">CVE-2022-29203</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault and OOB write due to incomplete validation in <code>EditDistance</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29208">CVE-2022-29208</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>Conv3DBackpropFilterV2</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29204">CVE-2022-29204</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a denial of service in <code>tf.ragged.constant</code> due to lack of validation (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29202">CVE-2022-29202</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault when <code>tf.histogram_fixed_width</code> is called with NaN values (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29211">CVE-2022-29211</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a core dump when loading TFLite models with quantization (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29212">CVE-2022-29212</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes crashes stemming from incomplete validation in signal ops (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29213">CVE-2022-29213</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a type confusion leading to <code>CHECK</code>-failure based denial of service (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29209">CVE-2022-29209</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap buffer overflow due to incorrect hash function (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29210">CVE-2022-29210</a>)</li>
<li>Updates <code>curl</code> to <code>7.83.1</code> to handle (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-22576">CVE-2022-22576</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27774">CVE-2022-27774</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27775">CVE-2022-27775</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27776">CVE-2022-27776</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27778">CVE-2022-27778</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27779">CVE-2022-27779</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27780">CVE-2022-27780</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27781">CVE-2022-27781</a>, (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-27782">CVE-2022-27782</a> and (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=VE-2022-30115">CVE-2022-30115</a></li>
<li>Updates <code>zlib</code> to <code>1.2.12</code> after <code>1.2.11</code> was pulled due to <a href="https://www.openwall.com/lists/oss-security/2022/03/28/1">security issue</a></li>
</ul>

<h1>Release 2.8.1</h1>
<p>This releases introduces several vulnerability fixes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fixes a code injection in <code>saved_model_cli</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29216">CVE-2022-29216</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes <code>TensorSummaryV2</code> to crash (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29193">CVE-2022-29193</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which crashes <code>QuantizeAndDequantizeV4Grad</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29192">CVE-2022-29192</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>DeleteSessionTensor</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29194">CVE-2022-29194</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>GetSessionTensor</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29191">CVE-2022-29191</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>StagePeek</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29195">CVE-2022-29195</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>UnsortedSegmentJoin</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29197">CVE-2022-29197</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>LoadAndRemapMatrix</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29199">CVE-2022-29199</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>SparseTensorToCSRSparseMatrix</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29198">CVE-2022-29198</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>LSTMBlockCell</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29200">CVE-2022-29200</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which causes denial of service via <code>Conv3DBackpropFilterV2</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29196">CVE-2022-29196</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code> failure in depthwise ops via overflows (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-41197">CVE-2021-41197</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes issues arising from undefined behavior stemming from users supplying invalid resource handles (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29207">CVE-2022-29207</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault due to missing support for quantized types (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29205">CVE-2022-29205</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which results in undefined behavior in <code>SparseTensorDenseAdd</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29206">CVE-2022-29206</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a missing validation which results in undefined behavior in <code>QuantizedConv2D</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29201">CVE-2022-29201</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an integer overflow in <code>SpaceToBatchND</code> (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2022-29203">CVE-2022-29203</a>)</li>
