    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29614">CVE-2021-29614</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a stack overflow in <code>ParseAttrValue</code> with nested tensors
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29615">CVE-2021-29615</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a null dereference in Grappler's <code>TrySimplify</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29616">CVE-2021-29616</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a crash in <code>tf.transpose</code> with complex inputs
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29618">CVE-2021-29618</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a crash in <code>tf.strings.substr</code> due to <code>CHECK</code>-fail
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29617">CVE-2021-29617</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>tf.raw_ops.SparseCountSparseOutput</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29619">CVE-2021-29619</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>tf.raw_ops.ImmutableConst</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29539">CVE-2021-29539</a>)</li>
<li>Updates <code>curl</code> to <code>7.76.0</code> to handle
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-8169">CVE-2020-8169</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-8177">CVE-2020-8177</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-8231">CVE-2020-8231</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-8284">CVE-2020-8284</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-8285">CVE-2020-8285</a>
    and
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-8286">CVE-2020-8286</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h1>Release 2.5.0</h1>
<h2>Major Features and Improvements</h2>
<ul>
<li>Support for Python3.9 has been added.</li>
<li><code>tf.data</code>:<ul>
<li><code>tf.data</code> service now supports strict round-robin reads, which is useful
    for synchronous training workloads where example sizes vary. With strict
    round robin reads, users can guarantee that consumers get similar-sized
    examples in the same step.</li>
<li>tf.data service now supports optional compression. Previously data would
    always be compressed, but now you can disable compression by passing
    <code>compression=None</code> to <code>tf.data.experimental.service.distribute(...)</code>.</li>
<li><code>tf.data.Dataset.batch()</code> now supports <code>num_parallel_calls</code> and
    <code>deterministic</code> arguments. <code>num_parallel_calls</code> is used to indicate that
    multiple input batches should be computed in parallel. With
    <code>num_parallel_calls</code> set, <code>deterministic</code> is used to indicate that
    outputs can be obtained in the non-deterministic order.</li>
<li>Options returned by <code>tf.data.Dataset.options()</code> are no longer mutable.</li>
<li>tf.data input pipelines can now be executed in debug mode, which
    disables any asynchrony, parallelism, or non-determinism and forces
    Python execution (as opposed to trace-compiled graph execution) of
    user-defined functions passed into transformations such as <code>map</code>. The
    debug mode can be enabled through
    <code>tf.data.experimental.enable_debug_mode()</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.lite</code><ul>
<li>Enabled the new MLIR-based quantization backend by default<ul>
<li>The new backend is used for 8 bits full integer post-training
    quantization</li>
<li>The new backend removes the redundant rescales and fixes some bugs
    (shared weight/bias, extremely small scales, etc)</li>
<li>Set <code>experimental_new_quantizer</code> in tf.lite.TFLiteConverter to False
    to disable this change</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.keras</code><ul>
<li><code>tf.keras.metrics.AUC</code> now support logit predictions.</li>
<li>Enabled a new supported input type in <code>Model.fit</code>,
    <code>tf.keras.utils.experimental.DatasetCreator</code>, which takes a callable,
    <code>dataset_fn</code>. <code>DatasetCreator</code> is intended to work across all
    <code>tf.distribute</code> strategies, and is the only input type supported for
    Parameter Server strategy.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.distribute</code><ul>
<li><code>tf.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code> now supports
    training with Keras <code>Model.fit</code> when used with <code>DatasetCreator</code>.</li>
<li>Creating <code>tf.random.Generator</code> under <code>tf.distribute.Strategy</code> scopes is
    now allowed (except for
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.CentralStorageStrategy</code> and
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code>). Different
    replicas will get different random-number streams.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>TPU embedding support<ul>
<li>Added <code>profile_data_directory</code> to <code>EmbeddingConfigSpec</code> in
    <code>_tpu_estimator_embedding.py</code>. This allows embedding lookup statistics
    gathered at runtime to be used in embedding layer partitioning
    decisions.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>PluggableDevice<ul>
<li>Third-party devices can now connect to TensorFlow as plug-ins through
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/blob/master/rfcs/20200612-stream-executor-c-api.md">StreamExecutor C API</a>.
    and
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/blob/master/rfcs/20200624-pluggable-device-for-tensorflow.md">PluggableDevice</a>
    interface.<ul>
<li>Add custom ops and kernels through
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/blob/master/rfcs/20190814-kernel-and-op-registration.md">kernel and op registration C API</a>.</li>
<li>Register custom graph optimization passes with
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/community/blob/master/rfcs/20201027-modular-tensorflow-graph-c-api.md">graph optimization C API</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/oneapi-src/oneDNN">oneAPI Deep Neural Network Library (oneDNN)</a>
    CPU performance optimizations from
    <a href="https://software.intel.com/content/www/us/en/develop/articles/intel-optimization-for-tensorflow-installation-guide.html">Intel-optimized TensorFlow</a>
    are now available in the official x86-64 Linux and Windows builds.<ul>
<li>They are off by default. Enable them by setting the environment variable
    <code>TF_ENABLE_ONEDNN_OPTS=1</code>.</li>
<li>We do not recommend using them in GPU systems, as they have not been
    sufficiently tested with GPUs yet.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>TensorFlow pip packages are now built with CUDA11.2 and cuDNN 8.1.0</li>
</ul>
<h2>Breaking Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>The <code>TF_CPP_MIN_VLOG_LEVEL</code> environment variable has been renamed to
    <code>TF_CPP_MAX_VLOG_LEVEL</code> which correctly describes its effect.</li>
</ul>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Preprocessing layers API consistency changes:<ul>
<li><code>StringLookup</code> added <code>output_mode</code>, <code>sparse</code>, and
    <code>pad_to_max_tokens</code> arguments with same semantics as
    <code>TextVectorization</code>.</li>
<li><code>IntegerLookup</code> added <code>output_mode</code>, <code>sparse</code>, and
    <code>pad_to_max_tokens</code> arguments with same semantics as
    <code>TextVectorization</code>. Renamed <code>max_values</code>, <code>oov_value</code> and
    <code>mask_value</code> to <code>max_tokens</code>, <code>oov_token</code> and <code>mask_token</code> to align
    with <code>StringLookup</code> and <code>TextVectorization</code>.</li>
<li><code>TextVectorization</code> default for <code>pad_to_max_tokens</code> switched to
    False.</li>
<li><code>CategoryEncoding</code> no longer supports <code>adapt</code>, <code>IntegerLookup</code> now
    supports equivalent functionality. <code>max_tokens</code> argument renamed to
    <code>num_tokens</code>.</li>
<li><code>Discretization</code> added <code>num_bins</code> argument for learning bins
    boundaries through calling <code>adapt</code> on a dataset. Renamed <code>bins</code>
    argument to <code>bin_boundaries</code> for specifying bins without <code>adapt</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Improvements to model saving/loading:<ul>
<li><code>model.load_weights</code> now accepts paths to saved models.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Keras inputs can now be created directly from arbitrary <code>tf.TypeSpecs</code>.</li>
<li>Two new learning rate schedules added:
    <code>tf.keras.optimizers.schedules.CosineDecay</code>
    and<code>tf.keras.optimizers.schedules.CosineDecayRestarts</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Exposing <code>tf.data.experimental.ExternalStatePolicy</code>, which can be used
    to control how external state should be handled during dataset
    serialization or iterator checkpointing.</li>
<li>Changing <code>tf.data.experimental.save</code> to store the type specification of
    the dataset elements. This avoids the need for explicitly specifying the
    <code>element_spec</code> argument of <code>tf.data.experimental.load</code> when loading the
    previously saved dataset.</li>
<li>Add <code>.element_spec</code> property to <code>tf.data.DatasetSpec</code> to access the
    inner spec. This can be used to extract the structure of nested
    datasets.</li>
<li>Add <code>tf.data.experimental.AutoShardingPolicy.HINT</code> which can be used to
    provide hints to tf.distribute-based auto-sharding as to where in the
    input pipeline to insert sharding transformations.</li>
<li>Make tf.data.Options persistent across <code>tf.function</code> and <code>GraphDef</code>
    boundaries.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>XLA compilation:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.function(experimental_compile=True)</code> has become a stable API,
    renamed <code>tf.function(jit_compile=True)</code>.</li>
<li>XLA can now compile MirroredStrategy: the step function passed
    to<code>strategy.run</code> can now be annoted with <code>jit_compile=True</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.distribute</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Rename <code>experimental_prefetch_to_device</code> in <code>tf.distribute.InputOptions</code>
    to <code>experimental_fetch_to_device</code> to better reflect the purpose.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>class <code>tflite::Subgraph</code>:<ul>
<li>Removed the <code>tensors()</code> method and the non-const overload of the
    <code>nodes_and_registration()</code> method, both of which were previously
    documented as temporary and to be removed.<ul>
<li>Uses of <code>tensors()</code> can be replaced by calling the existing
    methods <code>tensors_size()</code> and <code>tensor(int)</code>.</li>
<li>Uses of the non-const overload of <code>nodes_and_registration</code> can
    be replaced by calling the existing methods <code>nodes_size()</code> and
    <code>context()</code>, and then calling the <code>GetNodeAndRegistration</code>
    method in the <code>TfLiteContext</code> returned by <code>context()</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>NNAPI<ul>
<li>Removed deprecated <code>Interpreter::UseNNAPI(bool)</code> C++ API.<ul>
<li>Use <code>NnApiDelegate()</code> and related delegate configuration methods
    directly.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Replaced the model cache key for models computation algorithm with
    one guaranteed to be stable across runs.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>16 bits quantization<ul>
<li>Added int16x8 support for ABS, REDUCE_MAX and REDUCE_MIN operators.</li>
<li>Additional tests and fixes for ADD and SUB operators.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Added support for saved model's session initializer through
    <code>TFLiteConverter.from_saved_model</code>.</li>
<li>Added DEPTH_TO_SPACE support in Post training quantization.</li>
<li>Added dynamic range quantization support for the BatchMatMul op.<ul>
<li>Both symmetric and asymmetric quantized input tensor are supported.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Add <code>RFFT2D</code> as builtin op. (<code>RFFT2D</code> also supports <code>RFFTD</code>.) Currently
    only supports float32 input.</li>
<li>Add 5D support to <code>SLICE</code> op.</li>
<li>TFLite Supports SingatureDef:<ul>
<li>TFLiteConverter exports models with SignatureDef</li>
<li>Interpreter supports getting a list of signatures and getting
    callable function for a given signaturedef.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Add int8 support for <code>ReshapeV2</code>.</li>
<li>Add experimental support for optimization with sparsity.</li>
<li>Add nominal support for unsigned 32-bit integer tensor types. Note that
    very few TFLite kernels support this type natively, so its use in mobile
    ML authoring is generally discouraged.</li>
<li>Add support for static hash tables through
    <code>TFLiteConverter.from_saved_model</code>.</li>
<li>The Python TF Lite Interpreter bindings now has an option
    <code>experimental_preserve_all_tensors</code> to aid in debugging conversion.</li>
<li>Quantized x86 execution defaults to Ruy GEMM library for platforms with
    AVX support.</li>
<li>Deprecate
    <code>tf.compat.v1.lite.experimental.get_potentially_supported_ops</code>. Use
    <code>tf.lite.TFLiteConverter</code> directly to check whether a model is
    convertible.</li>
<li>Add support to select one of three different built-in op resolvers</li>
<li>Enabled post training with calibrations for models that require user
    provided TensorFlow Lite custom op libraries via
    <code>converter.target_spec._experimental_custom_op_registerers</code>. used in
    Python Interpreter API.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>TF Core:</p>
<ul>
<li>Corrected higher-order gradients of control flow constructs (<code>tf.cond</code>,
    <code>tf.while_loop</code>, and compositions like <code>tf.foldl</code>) computed with
    <code>tf.GradientTape</code> inside a <code>tf.function</code>.</li>
<li>Changed the default step size in <code>gradient_checker_v2.compute_gradients</code>
    to be exactly representable as a binary floating point numbers. This
    avoids poluting gradient approximations needlessly, which is some cases
    leads to false negatives in op gradient tests.</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.config.experimental.get_memory_info</code>, returning a dict with
    the current and peak memory usage. Deprecated
    <code>tf.config.experimental.get_memory_usage</code> in favor of this new function.</li>
<li>Extended <code>tf.config.experimental.enable_tensor_float_32_execution</code> to
    control Tensor-Float-32 evaluation in RNNs.</li>
<li>Added a 'experimental_payloads' field to tf.errors.OpError and its
    subclasses to support more detailed error reporting. This is inspired
    from Abseil Status payloads:
    https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/status/status.h</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.summary</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>New <code>tf.summary.graph</code> allows manual write of TensorFlow graph
    (<code>tf.Graph</code> or <code>tf.compat.v1.GraphDef</code>) as a summary. This is not a
    replacement for the trace-based API.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Set <code>/d2ReducedOptimizeHugeFunctions</code> by default for Windows builds. This
    provides a big compile-time speedup, and effectively raises the minimum
    supported MSVC version to 16.4 (current: 16.8).</p>
<ul>
<li>See:
    https://groups.google.com/a/tensorflow.org/d/topic/build/SsW98Eo7l3o/discussion</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>TensorRT</p>
<ul>
<li>Removed the deprecated <code>session_config</code> parameter for the TF1-TRT
    converter <code>TrtGraphConverter</code>. Previously, we issued a warning when the
    value of the parameter is not None.</li>
<li>The TF2-TRT converter <code>TrtGraphConverterV2</code> takes an object of class
    TrtConversionParams as a parameter. Removed three deprecated fields from
    this class: <code>rewriter_config_template</code>, <code>is_dynamic_op</code>, and
    <code>max_batch_size</code>. Previously, we issued a warning when the value of
    <code>rewriter_config_template</code> is not None. We issued an error when the
    value of <code>is_dynamic_op</code> is not True. We didn't use the value for
    <code>max_batch_size</code> for building TensorRT engines. Add parameters
    <code>use_dynamic_shape</code> to enable dynamic shape support. The default is to
    disable dynamic shape support. Add <code>dynamic_shape_profile_strategy</code> for
    selecting a dynamic shape profile strategy. The default is profile
    strategy is <code>Range</code>.</li>
<li>Issue a warning when function get_tensorrt_rewriter_config is used.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>TF XLA</p>
<ul>
<li>Add new enum value <code>MLIR_BRIDGE_ROLLOUT_SAFE_MODE_ENABLED</code> to
    <code>tf.config.experimental.mlir_bridge_rollout</code> to enable a \"safe\" mode.
    This runs the MLIR bridge only when an analysis of the graph only when
    an analysis of the graph determines that it is safe to run.</li>
<li>Add new enum value <code>MLIR_BRIDGE_ROLLOUT_SAFE_MODE_FALLBACK_ENABLED'
    to</code>tf.config.experimental.mlir_bridge_rollout` to enable a fallback for
    the MLIR bridge in a \"safe\" mode. This runs the MLIR bridge in a
    FallbackEnabled mode when an analysis of the graph determines that the
    graph does not have unsupported features.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deterministic Op Functionality:</p>
<ul>
<li>Add determinism-unimplemented exception-throwing to the segment-sum ops.
    When the environment variable <code>TF_DETERMINISTIC_OPS</code> is set to <code>"true"</code>
    or <code>"1"</code> (when op-determinism is expected), an attempt to run the
    following ops on a GPU will throw <code>tf.errors.UnimplementedError</code> (with
    an understandable message) when <code>data</code> is a floating-point type,
    including complex types (if supported): <code>tf.math.segment_prod</code>,
    <code>tf.math.segment_sum</code>, <code>tf.math.unsorted_segment_mean</code>,
    <code>tf.math.unsorted_segment_sqrt_n</code>, <code>tf.math.unsorted_segment_prod</code>,
    <code>tf.math.unsorted_segment_sum</code>, and therefore also
    <code>tf.convert_to_tensor</code> when <code>value</code> is of type <code>tf.IndexedSlices</code> (such
    as in the back prop though <code>tf.gather</code> into a dense embedding). See
    issue <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/39751">39751</a>
    which this change addresses, but does not solve. This exception-throwing
    behavior can be disabled by setting the environment variable
    <code>TF_DISABLE_SEGMENT_REDUCTION_OP_DETERMINISM_EXCEPTIONS</code> to <code>"true"</code> or
    <code>"1"</code>. For more information about these changes, see the description in
    pull request
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/pull/47772">47772</a>.</li>
<li>In previous versions of TensorFlow, when a GPU was available,
    <code>tf.sparse.sparse_dense_matmul</code> introduced truly random noise in the
    forward path for data of type <code>tf.float32</code> but not for data of type
    <code>tf.float64</code> (for which there was no GPU implementation). In this
    current release, GPU support for other floating-point types
    (<code>tf.float16</code>, <code>tf.float64</code>, <code>tf.complex64</code>, and <code>tf.complex128</code>) has
    been added for this op. If you were relying on the determinism of the
    <code>tf.float64</code> CPU implementation being automatically selected because of
    the absence of the <code>tf.float64</code> GPU implementation, you with either need
    to force the op to run on the CPU or use a different data type.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Security</p>
<ul>
<li>Fixes a heap buffer overflow in <code>RaggedBinCount</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29512">CVE-2021-29512</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap out of bounds write in <code>RaggedBinCount</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29514">CVE-2021-29514</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a type confusion during tensor casts which leads to dereferencing
    null pointers
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29513">CVE-2021-29513</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a reference binding to null pointer in <code>MatrixDiag*</code> ops
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29515">CVE-2021-29515</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a null pointer dereference via invalid Ragged Tensors
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29516">CVE-2021-29516</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by zero in <code>Conv3D</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29517">CVE-2021-29517</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes vulnerabilities where session operations in eager mode lead to
    null pointer dereferences
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29518">CVE-2021-29518</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code>-fail in <code>SparseCross</code> caused by type confusion
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29519">CVE-2021-29519</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>SparseCountSparseOutput</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29521">CVE-2021-29521</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap buffer overflow in <code>Conv3DBackprop*</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29520">CVE-2021-29520</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by 0 in <code>Conv3DBackprop*</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29522">CVE-2021-29522</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code>-fail in <code>AddManySparseToTensorsMap</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29523">CVE-2021-29523</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by 0 in <code>Conv2DBackpropFilter</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29524">CVE-2021-29524</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by 0 in <code>Conv2DBackpropInput</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29525">CVE-2021-29525</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by 0 in <code>Conv2D</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29526">CVE-2021-29526</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by 0 in <code>QuantizedConv2D</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29527">CVE-2021-29527</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a division by 0 in <code>QuantizedMul</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-29528">CVE-2021-29528</a>)</li>

<h1>Release 2.4.1</h1>
<ul>
<li>This release removes the AVX2 requirement from TF 2.4.0.</li>
</ul>
<h1>Release 2.3.2</h1>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>Fixes an access to unitialized memory in Eigen code
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26266">CVE-2020-26266</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a security vulnerability caused by lack of validation in
    <code>tf.raw_ops.DataFormatVecPermute</code> and <code>tf.raw_ops.DataFormatDimMap</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26267">CVE-2020-26267</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a vulnerability caused by attempting to write to immutable memory
    region in <code>tf.raw_ops.ImmutableConst</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26268">CVE-2020-26268</a></li>
<li>Fixes a <code>CHECK</code>-fail in LSTM with zero-length input
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26270">CVE-2020-26270</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a security vulnerability caused by accessing heap data outside of
    bounds when loading a specially crafted <code>SavedModel</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26271">CVE-2020-26271</a>)</li>
<li>Solves an OOM issue on TPUs when XLA contexts use fused average updates</li>
<li>Updates <code>libjpeg-turbo</code> to <code>2.0.5</code> to handle
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13790">CVE-2020-13790</a>.</li>
<li>Updates <code>junit</code> to <code>4.13.1</code> to handle
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15250">CVE-2020-15250</a>.</li>
<li>Updates <code>PCRE</code> to <code>8.44</code> to handle
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2019-20838">CVE-2019-20838</a>
    and
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-14155">CVE-2020-14155</a>.</li>
<li>Updates <code>sqlite3</code> to <code>3.44.0</code> to keep in sync with master branch.</li>
</ul>

<h1>Release 2.4.0</h1>
<p>## Major Features and Improvements</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>tf.distribute</code> introduces experimental support for asynchronous training of
    models via the
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/distribute/experimental/ParameterServerStrategy"><code>tf.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code></a>
    API. Please see the
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/tutorials/distribute/parameter_server_training">tutorial</a>
    to learn more.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/distribute/MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy"><code>MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy</code></a>
    is now a stable API and is no longer considered experimental. Some of the
    major improvements involve handling peer failure and many bug fixes. Please
    check out the detailed tutorial on
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/tutorials/distribute/multi_worker_with_keras">Multi-worker training with Keras</a>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Introduces experimental support for a new module named
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/experimental/numpy"><code>tf.experimental.numpy</code></a>
    which is a NumPy-compatible API for writing TF programs. See the
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/guide/tf_numpy">detailed guide</a> to learn more.
    Additional details below.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Adds Support for
    <a href="https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/2020/05/14/tensorfloat-32-precision-format/">TensorFloat-32</a>
    on Ampere based GPUs. TensorFloat-32, or TF32 for short, is a math mode for
    NVIDIA Ampere based GPUs and is enabled by default.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A major refactoring of the internals of the Keras Functional API has been
    completed, that should improve the reliability, stability, and performance
    of constructing Functional models.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keras mixed precision API
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/mixed_precision?version=nightly"><code>tf.keras.mixed_precision</code></a>
    is no longer experimental and allows the use of 16-bit floating point
    formats during training, improving performance by up to 3x on GPUs and 60%
    on TPUs. Please see below for additional details.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TensorFlow Profiler now supports profiling <code>MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy</code> and
    tracing multiple workers using the
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/guide/profiler#profiling_apis">sampling mode API</a>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TFLite Profiler for Android is available. See the detailed
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/lite/performance/measurement#trace_tensorflow_lite_internals_in_android">guide</a>
    to learn more.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TensorFlow pip packages are now built with CUDA11 and cuDNN 8.0.2.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Breaking Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>
<p>TF Core:</p>
<ul>
<li>Certain float32 ops run in lower precision on Ampere based GPUs,
    including matmuls and convolutions, due to the use of
    <a href="https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/2020/05/14/tensorfloat-32-precision-format/">TensorFloat-32</a>.
    Specifically, inputs to such ops are rounded from 23 bits of precision
    to 10 bits of precision. This is unlikely to cause issues in practice
    for deep learning models. In some cases, TensorFloat-32 is also used for
    complex64 ops. TensorFloat-32 can be disabled by running
    <code>tf.config.experimental.enable_tensor_float_32_execution(False)</code>.</li>
<li>The byte layout for string tensors across the C-API has been updated to
    match TF Core/C++; i.e., a contiguous array of
    <code>tensorflow::tstring</code>/<code>TF_TString</code>s.</li>
<li>C-API functions <code>TF_StringDecode</code>, <code>TF_StringEncode</code>, and
    <code>TF_StringEncodedSize</code> are no longer relevant and have been removed; see
    <code>core/platform/ctstring.h</code> for string access/modification in C.</li>
<li><code>tensorflow.python</code>, <code>tensorflow.core</code> and <code>tensorflow.compiler</code> modules
    are now hidden. These modules are not part of TensorFlow public API.</li>
<li><code>tf.raw_ops.Max</code> and <code>tf.raw_ops.Min</code> no longer accept inputs of type
    <code>tf.complex64</code> or <code>tf.complex128</code>, because the behavior of these ops is
    not well defined for complex types.</li>
<li>XLA:CPU and XLA:GPU devices are no longer registered by default. Use
    <code>TF_XLA_FLAGS=--tf_xla_enable_xla_devices</code> if you really need them, but
    this flag will eventually be removed in subsequent releases.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.keras</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <code>steps_per_execution</code> argument in <code>model.compile()</code> is no longer
    experimental; if you were passing <code>experimental_steps_per_execution</code>,
    rename it to <code>steps_per_execution</code> in your code. This argument controls
    the number of batches to run during each <code>tf.function</code> call when calling
    <code>model.fit()</code>. Running multiple batches inside a single <code>tf.function</code>
    call can greatly improve performance on TPUs or small models with a
    large Python overhead.</li>
<li>A <strong>major refactoring</strong> of the internals of the Keras Functional API may
    affect code that is relying on certain internal details:</li>
<li>Code that uses <code>isinstance(x, tf.Tensor)</code> instead of <code>tf.is_tensor</code> when
    checking Keras symbolic inputs/outputs should switch to using
    <code>tf.is_tensor</code>.</li>
<li>Code that is overly dependent on the exact names attached to symbolic
    tensors (e.g. assumes there will be ":0" at the end of the inputs,
    treats names as unique identifiers instead of using <code>tensor.ref()</code>,
    etc.) may break.</li>
<li>Code that uses full path for <code>get_concrete_function</code> to trace Keras
    symbolic inputs directly should switch to building matching
    <code>tf.TensorSpec</code>s directly and tracing the <code>TensorSpec</code> objects.</li>
<li>Code that relies on the exact number and names of the op layers that
    TensorFlow operations were converted into may have changed.</li>
<li>Code that uses <code>tf.map_fn</code>/<code>tf.cond</code>/<code>tf.while_loop</code>/control flow as op
    layers and happens to work before TF 2.4. These will explicitly be
    unsupported now. Converting these ops to Functional API op layers was
    unreliable before TF 2.4, and prone to erroring incomprehensibly or
    being silently buggy.</li>
<li>Code that directly asserts on a Keras symbolic value in cases where ops
    like <code>tf.rank</code> used to return a static or symbolic value depending on if
    the input had a fully static shape or not. Now these ops always return
    symbolic values.</li>
<li>Code already susceptible to leaking tensors outside of graphs becomes
    slightly more likely to do so now.</li>
<li>Code that tries directly getting gradients with respect to symbolic
    Keras inputs/outputs. Use <code>GradientTape</code> on the actual Tensors passed to
    the already-constructed model instead.</li>
<li>Code that requires very tricky shape manipulation via converted op
    layers in order to work, where the Keras symbolic shape inference proves
    insufficient.</li>
<li>Code that tries manually walking a <code>tf.keras.Model</code> layer by layer and
    assumes layers only ever have one positional argument. This assumption
    doesn't hold true before TF 2.4 either, but is more likely to cause
    issues now.</li>
<li>Code that manually enters <code>keras.backend.get_graph()</code> before building a
    functional model is no longer needed.</li>
<li>Start enforcing input shape assumptions when calling Functional API
    Keras models. This may potentially break some users, in case there is a
    mismatch between the shape used when creating <code>Input</code> objects in a
    Functional model, and the shape of the data passed to that model. You
    can fix this mismatch by either calling the model with correctly-shaped
    data, or by relaxing <code>Input</code> shape assumptions (note that you can pass
    shapes with <code>None</code> entries for axes that are meant to be dynamic). You
    can also disable the input checking entirely by setting
    <code>model.input_spec = None</code>.</li>
<li>Several changes have been made to
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental</code>. Note that it is now recommended
    to use the non-experimental <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision</code> API.</li>
<li><code>AutoCastVariable.dtype</code> now refers to the actual variable dtype, not
    the dtype it will be casted to.</li>
<li>When mixed precision is enabled, <code>tf.keras.layers.Embedding</code> now outputs
    a float16 or bfloat16 tensor instead of a float32 tensor.</li>
<li>The property
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScaleOptimizer.loss_scale</code> is
    now a tensor, not a <code>LossScale</code> object. This means to get a loss scale
    of a <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code> as a tensor, you must now call
    <code>opt.loss_scale</code>instead of <code>opt.loss_scale()</code>.</li>
<li>The property <code>should_cast_variables</code> has been removed from
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.Policy</code></li>
<li>When passing a <code>tf.mixed_precision.experimental.DynamicLossScale</code> to
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScaleOptimizer</code>, the
    <code>DynamicLossScale</code>'s multiplier must be 2.</li>
<li>When passing a <code>tf.mixed_precision.experimental.DynamicLossScale</code> to
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScaleOptimizer</code>, the weights
    of the <code>DynanmicLossScale</code> are copied into the <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code>
    instead of being reused. This means modifying the weights of the
    <code>DynamicLossScale</code> will no longer affect the weights of the
    LossScaleOptimizer, and vice versa.</li>
<li>The global policy can no longer be set to a non-floating point policy in
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.set_policy</code></li>
<li>In <code>Layer.call</code>, <code>AutoCastVariable</code>s will no longer be casted within
    <code>MirroredStrategy.run</code> or <code>ReplicaContext.merge_call</code>. This is because a
    thread local variable is used to determine whether <code>AutoCastVariable</code>s
    are casted, and those two functions run with a different thread. Note
    this only applies if one of these two functions is called within
    <code>Layer.call</code>; if one of those two functions calls <code>Layer.call</code>,
    <code>AutoCastVariable</code>s will still be casted.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.data</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.data.experimental.service.DispatchServer</code> now takes a config tuple
    instead of individual arguments. Usages should be updated to
    <code>tf.data.experimental.service.DispatchServer(dispatcher_config)</code>.</li>
<li><code>tf.data.experimental.service.WorkerServer</code> now takes a config tuple
    instead of individual arguments. Usages should be updated to
    <code>tf.data.experimental.service.WorkerServer(worker_config)</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.distribute</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Removes <code>tf.distribute.Strategy.experimental_make_numpy_dataset</code>. Please
    use <code>tf.data.Dataset.from_tensor_slices</code> instead.</li>
<li>Renames <code>experimental_hints</code> in
    <code>tf.distribute.StrategyExtended.reduce_to</code>,
    <code>tf.distribute.StrategyExtended.batch_reduce_to</code>,
    <code>tf.distribute.ReplicaContext.all_reduce</code> to <code>options</code>.</li>
<li>Renames <code>tf.distribute.experimental.CollectiveHints</code> to
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.CommunicationOptions</code>.</li>
<li>Renames <code>tf.distribute.experimental.CollectiveCommunication</code> to
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.CommunicationImplementation</code>.</li>
<li>Renames
    <code>tf.distribute.Strategy.experimental_distribute_datasets_from_function</code>
    to <code>distribute_datasets_from_function</code> as it is no longer experimental.</li>
<li>Removes <code>tf.distribute.Strategy.experimental_run_v2</code> method, which was
    deprecated in TF 2.2.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>tf.lite</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.quantization.quantize_and_dequantize_v2</code> has been introduced, which
    updates the gradient definition for quantization which is outside the
    range to be 0. To simulate the V1 the behavior of
    <code>tf.quantization.quantize_and_dequantize(...)</code> use
    <code>tf.grad_pass_through(tf.quantization.quantize_and_dequantize_v2)(...)</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Building TensorFlow:</p>
<ul>
<li>Windows platform builds: TensorFlow on Windows under MSVC is now built
    with <code>--copt=/experimental:preprocessor
    --host_copt=/experimental:preprocessor</code> (see <code>.bazelrc</code> for more
    details). Builds including TensorFlow may fail with unexpected syntax
    errors if these flags are absent. See also
    <a href="https://groups.google.com/a/tensorflow.org/g/build/c/LbAw8RILvTg/m/ttnuhYU2BgAJ">this thread on SIG Build</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Known Caveats</h2>
<ul>
<li><code>tf.keras.mixed_precision</code><ul>
<li>When using mixed precision, calling <code>RMSprop.apply_gradients</code> or
    <code>Nadam.apply_gradients</code> outside a <code>tf.function</code> does not work and will
    raise the AttributeError "Tensor.op is meaningless when eager execution
    is enabled". See this
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/45536">issue</a> for
    details and a workaround.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<h3>TF Core:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Introduces experimental support for a new module named
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/experimental/numpy"><code>tf.experimental.numpy</code></a>,
    which is a NumPy-compatible API for writing TF programs. This module
    provides class <code>ndarray</code>, which mimics the <code>ndarray</code> class in NumPy, and
    wraps an immutable <code>tf.Tensor</code> under the hood. A subset of NumPy functions
    (e.g. <code>numpy.add</code>) are provided. Their inter-operation with TF facilities is
    seamless in most cases. See
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/blob/master/tensorflow/python/ops/numpy_ops/README.md">tensorflow/python/ops/numpy_ops/README.md</a>
    for details of what operations are supported and what are the differences
    from NumPy.</li>
<li><code>tf.types.experimental.TensorLike</code> is a new <code>Union</code> type that can be used as
    type annotation for variables representing a Tensor or a value that can be
    converted to Tensor by <code>tf.convert_to_tensor</code>.</li>
<li>Calling ops with a python constants or numpy values is now consistent with
    tf.convert_to_tensor behavior. This avoids operations like tf.reshape
    truncating inputs such as from int64 to int32.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.sparse.map_values</code> to apply a function to the <code>.value</code>s of
    <code>SparseTensor</code> arguments.</li>
<li>The Python bitwise operators for <code>Tensor</code> (<code>__and__</code>, <code>__or__</code>, <code>__xor__</code>
    and <code>__invert__</code> now support non-<code>bool</code> arguments and apply the
    corresponding bitwise ops. <code>bool</code> arguments continue to be supported and
    dispatch to logical ops. This brings them more in line with Python and NumPy
    behavior.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.SparseTensor.with_values</code>. This returns a new SparseTensor with the
    same sparsity pattern, but with new provided values. It is similar to the
    <code>with_values</code> function of <code>RaggedTensor</code>.</li>
<li>Adds <code>StatelessCase</code> op, and uses it if none of case branches has stateful
    ops.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.config.experimental.get_memory_usage</code> to return total memory usage
    of the device.</li>
<li>Adds gradients for <code>RaggedTensorToVariant</code> and <code>RaggedTensorFromVariant</code>.</li>
<li>Improve shape inference of nested function calls by supporting constant
    folding across Arg nodes which makes more static values available to shape
    inference functions.</li>
<li><code>tf.debugging</code>:<ul>
<li><code>tf.debugging.assert_shapes()</code> now works on <code>SparseTensor</code>s (Fixes
    <a href="https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/issues/36268">#36268</a>).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>GPU<ul>
<li>Adds Support for
    <a href="https://blogs.nvidia.com/blog/2020/05/14/tensorfloat-32-precision-format/">TensorFloat-32</a>
    on Ampere based GPUs.TensorFloat-32, or TF32 for short, is a math mode
    for NVIDIA Ampere based GPUs which causes certain float32 ops, such as
    matrix multiplications and convolutions, to run much faster on Ampere
    GPUs but with reduced precision. This reduced precision has not been
    found to effect convergence quality of deep learning models in practice.
    TensorFloat-32 is enabled by default, but can be disabled with
    <code>tf.config.experimental.enable_tensor_float_32_execution</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.math</code>:<ul>
<li>Adds <code>tf.math.erfcinv</code>, the inverse to <code>tf.math.erfc</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.nn</code>:<ul>
<li><code>tf.nn.max_pool2d</code> now supports explicit padding.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.image</code>:<ul>
<li>Adds deterministic <code>tf.image.stateless_random_*</code> functions for each
    <code>tf.image.random_*</code> function. Added a new op
    <code>stateless_sample_distorted_bounding_box</code> which is a deterministic
    version of <code>sample_distorted_bounding_box</code> op. Given the same seed,
    these stateless functions/ops produce the same results independent of
    how many times the function is called, and independent of global seed
    settings.</li>
<li>Adds deterministic <code>tf.image.resize</code> backprop CUDA kernels for
    <code>method=ResizeMethod.BILINEAR</code> (the default method). Enable by setting
    the environment variable <code>TF_DETERMINISTIC_OPS</code> to <code>"true"</code> or <code>"1"</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.print</code>:<ul>
<li>Bug fix in <code>tf.print()</code> with <code>OrderedDict</code> where if an <code>OrderedDict</code>
    didn't have the keys sorted, the keys and values were not being printed
    in accordance with their correct mapping.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>tf.train.Checkpoint</code>:<ul>
<li>Now accepts a <code>root</code> argument in the initialization, which generates a
    checkpoint with a root object. This allows users to create a
    <code>Checkpoint</code> object that is compatible with Keras <code>model.save_weights()</code>
    and <code>model.load_weights</code>. The checkpoint is also compatible with the
    checkpoint saved in the <code>variables/</code> folder in the SavedModel.</li>
<li>When restoring, <code>save_path</code> can be a path to a SavedModel. The function
    will automatically find the checkpoint in the SavedModel.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><code>tf.data</code>:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Adds new <code>tf.data.experimental.service.register_dataset</code> and
    <code>tf.data.experimental.service.from_dataset_id</code> APIs to enable one process to
    register a dataset with the tf.data service, and another process to consume
    data from the dataset.</li>
<li>Adds support for dispatcher fault tolerance. To enable fault tolerance,
    configure a <code>work_dir</code> when running your dispatcher server and set
    <code>dispatcher_fault_tolerance=True</code>. The dispatcher will store its state to
    <code>work_dir</code>, so that on restart it can continue from its previous state after
    restart.</li>
<li>Adds support for sharing dataset graphs via shared filesystem instead of
    over RPC. This reduces load on the dispatcher, improving performance of
    distributing datasets. For this to work, the dispatcher's <code>work_dir</code> must be
    accessible from workers. If the worker fails to read from the <code>work_dir</code>, it
    falls back to using RPC for dataset graph transfer.</li>
<li>Adds support for a new "distributed_epoch" processing mode. This processing
    mode distributes a dataset across all tf.data workers, instead of having
    each worker process the full dataset. See
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/data/experimental/service#understand_processing_mode">the tf.data service docs</a>
    to learn more.</li>
<li>Adds optional <code>exclude_cols</code> parameter to CsvDataset. This parameter is the
    complement of <code>select_cols</code>; at most one of these should be specified.</li>
<li>We have implemented an optimization which reorders data-discarding
    transformations such as <code>take</code> and <code>shard</code> to happen earlier in the dataset
    when it is safe to do so. The optimization can be disabled via the
    <code>experimental_optimization.reorder_data_discarding_ops</code> dataset option.</li>
<li><code>tf.data.Options</code> were previously immutable and can now be overridden.</li>
<li><code>tf.data.Dataset.from_generator</code> now supports Ragged and Sparse tensors with
    a new <code>output_signature</code> argument, which allows <code>from_generator</code> to produce
    any type describable by a <code>tf.TypeSpec</code>.</li>
<li><code>tf.data.experimental.AUTOTUNE</code> is now available in the core API as
    <code>tf.data.AUTOTUNE</code>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><code>tf.distribute</code>:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Introduces experimental support for asynchronous training of models via
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code>:<ul>
<li>Replaces the existing
    <code>tf.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code> symbol with a new
    class that is for parameter server training in TF2. Usage of the old
    symbol, usually with Estimator API, should be <strong>replaced</strong> with
    [<code>tf.compat.v1.distribute.experimental.ParameterServerStrategy</code>].</li>
<li>Added <code>tf.distribute.experimental.coordinator.*</code> namespace, including
    the main API <code>ClusterCoordinator</code> for coordinating the training cluster,
    the related data structure <code>RemoteValue</code> and <code>PerWorkerValue</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy</code>](https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/distribute/MultiWorkerMirroredStrategy)
    is now a stable API and is no longer considered experimental. Some of the
    major improvements involve handling peer failure and many bug fixes. Please
    check out the detailed tutorial on
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/tutorials/distribute/multi_worker_with_keras">Multi-worer training with Keras</a>.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.distribute.Strategy.gather</code> and
    <code>tf.distribute.ReplicaContext.all_gather</code> APIs to support gathering dense
    distributed values.</li>
<li>Fixes various issues with saving a distributed model.</li>
</ul>
<h3><code>tf.keras</code>:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Improvements from the Functional API refactoring:<ul>
<li>Functional model construction does not need to maintain a global
    workspace graph, removing memory leaks especially when building many
    models or very large models.</li>
<li>Functional model construction should be ~8-10% faster on average.</li>
<li>Functional models can now contain non-symbolic values in their call
    inputs inside of the first positional argument.</li>
<li>Several classes of TF ops that were not reliably converted to Keras
    layers during functional API construction should now work,
    e.g.<code>tf.image.ssim_multiscale</code></li>
<li>Error messages when Functional API construction goes wrong (and when ops
    cannot be converted to Keras layers automatically) should be clearer and
    easier to understand.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>Optimizer.minimize</code> can now accept a loss <code>Tensor</code> and a <code>GradientTape</code> as
    an alternative to accepting a <code>callable</code> loss.</li>
<li>Adds <code>beta</code> hyperparameter to
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/optimizers/Ftrl">FTRL</a>
    optimizer classes (Keras and others) to match
    <a href="https://research.google.com/pubs/archive/41159.pdf">FTRL paper</a>.</li>
<li><code>Optimizer.__init__</code> now accepts a <code>gradient_aggregator</code> to allow for
    customization of how gradients are aggregated across devices, as well as
    <code>gradients_transformers</code> to allow for custom gradient transformations (such
    as gradient clipping).</li>
<li>Improvements to Keras preprocessing layers:<ul>
<li>TextVectorization can now accept a vocabulary list or file as an init
    arg.</li>
<li>Normalization can now accept mean and variance values as init args.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>In <code>Attention</code> and <code>AdditiveAttention</code> layers, the <code>call()</code> method now
    accepts a <code>return_attention_scores</code> argument. When set to True, the layer
    returns the attention scores as an additional output argument.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.metrics.log_cosh</code> and <code>tf.metrics.logcosh</code> API entrypoints with the
    same implementation as their <code>tf.losses</code> equivalent.</li>
<li>For Keras model, the individual call of <code>Model.evaluate</code> uses no cached data
    for evaluation, while <code>Model.fit</code> uses cached data when <code>validation_data</code>
    arg is provided for better performance.</li>
<li>Adds a <code>save_traces</code> argument to <code>model.save</code>/ <code>tf.keras.models.save_model</code>
    which determines whether the SavedModel format stores the Keras model/layer
    call functions. The traced functions allow Keras to revive custom models and
    layers without the original class definition, but if this isn't required the
    tracing can be disabled with the added option.</li>
<li>The <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision</code> API is now non-experimental. The
    non-experimental API differs from the experimental API in several ways.<ul>
<li><code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.Policy</code> no longer takes in a
    <code>tf.mixed_precision. experimental.LossScale</code> in the constructor, and no
    longer has a <code>LossScale</code> associated with it. Instead, <code>Model.compile</code>
    will automatically wrap the optimizer with a <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code> using
    dynamic loss scaling if <code>Policy.name</code> is "mixed_float16".</li>
<li><code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.LossScaleOptimizer</code>'s constructor takes in
    different arguments. In particular, it no longer takes in a <code>LossScale</code>,
    and there is no longer a <code>LossScale</code> associated with the
    <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code>. Instead, <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code> directly implements
    fixed or dynamic loss scaling. See the documentation of
    <a href="https://www.tensorflow.org/api_docs/python/tf/keras/mixed_precision/experimental/LossScaleOptimizer?version=nightly"><code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScaleOptimizer</code></a>
    for details on the differences between the experimental
    <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code> and the new non-experimental <code>LossScaleOptimizer</code>.</li>
<li><code>tf.mixed_precision.experimental.LossScale</code> and its subclasses are
    deprecated, as all of its functionality now exists within
    <code>tf.keras.mixed_precision.LossScaleOptimizer</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><code>tf.lite</code>:</h3>
<ul>
<li><code>TFLiteConverter</code>:<ul>
<li>Support optional flags <code>inference_input_type</code> and
    <code>inference_output_type</code> for full integer quantized models. This allows
    users to modify the model input and output type to integer types
    (<code>tf.int8</code>, <code>tf.uint8</code>) instead of defaulting to float type
    (<code>tf.float32</code>).</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>NNAPI<ul>
<li>Adds NNAPI Delegation support for requantization use cases by converting
    the operation into a dequantize-quantize pair.</li>
<li>Removes deprecated <code>Interpreter.setUseNNAPI(boolean)</code> Java API. Use
    <code>Interpreter.Options.setUseNNAPI</code> instead.</li>
<li>Deprecates <code>Interpreter::UseNNAPI(bool)</code> C++ API. Use <code>NnApiDelegate()</code>
    and related delegate configuration methods directly.</li>
<li>Deprecates <code>Interpreter::SetAllowFp16PrecisionForFp32(bool)</code> C++ API.
    Prefer controlling this via delegate options, e.g.
    <code>tflite::StatefulNnApiDelegate::Options::allow_fp16'
    or</code>TfLiteGpuDelegateOptionsV2::is_precision_loss_allowed`.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>GPU<ul>
<li>GPU acceleration now supports quantized models by default</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>DynamicBuffer::AddJoinedString()</code> will now add a separator if the first
    string to be joined is empty.</li>
<li>Adds support for cumulative sum (cumsum), both as builtin op and MLIR
    conversion.</li>
</ul>
<h3><code>TensorRT</code></h3>
<ul>
<li>Issues a warning when the <code>session_config</code> parameter for the TF1 converter
    is used or the <code>rewrite_config_template</code> field in the TF2 converter
    parameter object is used.</li>
</ul>
<h3>TPU Enhancements:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Adds support for the <code>beta</code> parameter of the FTRL optimizer for TPU
    embeddings. Users of other TensorFlow platforms can implement equivalent
    behavior by adjusting the <code>l2</code> parameter.</li>
</ul>
<h3>XLA Support:</h3>
<ul>
<li>xla.experimental.compile is deprecated, use
    <code>tf.function(experimental_compile=True)</code> instead.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.function.experimental_get_compiler_ir</code> which returns compiler IR
    (currently 'hlo' and 'optimized_hlo') for given input for given function.</li>
</ul>
<h3>Security:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Fixes an undefined behavior causing a segfault in <code>tf.raw_ops.Switch</code>,
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15190">CVE-2020-15190</a>)</li>

<li><a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15192">CVE-2020-15192</a>,</li>
<li><a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15193">CVE-2020-15193</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Fixes two vulnerabilities in <code>SparseFillEmptyRowsGrad</code><ul>

</ul>
</li>
<li>Fixes several vulnerabilities in <code>RaggedCountSparseOutput</code> and
    <code>SparseCountSparseOutput</code> operations<ul>

<li><a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15198">CVE-2020-15198</a>,</li>

    API,
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15202">CVE-2020-15202</a>)</li>

    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15205">CVE-2020-15205</a>)</li>

    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15206">CVE-2020-15206</a>)</li>

    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15207">CVE-2020-15207</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a data corruption due to dimension mismatch in TFLite,
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15208">CVE-2020-15208</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes several vulnerabilities in TFLite saved model format<ul>

<li>Fixes a segfault in <code>tf.quantization.quantize_and_dequantize</code>,
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15265">CVE-2020-15265</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an undefined behavior float cast causing a crash,
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15266">CVE-2020-15266</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a lack of validation in <code>tf.raw_ops.DataFormatVecPermute</code> and
    <code>tf.raw_ops.DataFormatDimMap</code> which can cause uninitialized memory access,
    read outside bounds of arrays, data corruption and segmentation faults
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26267">CVE-2020-26267</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a crash caused by writing to read only memory region
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26268">CVE-2020-26268</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a heap out of bounds access in filesystem globbing implementation
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-26269">CVE-2020-26269</a>)</li>
</ul>
<h3>Other:</h3>
<ul>
<li>We have replaced uses of "whitelist" and "blacklist" with "allowlist" and
    "denylist" where possible. Please see
    <a href="https://developers.google.com/style/word-list#blacklist">this list</a> for
    more context.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.config.experimental.mlir_bridge_rollout</code> which will help us rollout
    the new MLIR TPU bridge.</li>
<li>Adds <code>tf.experimental.register_filesystem_plugin</code> to load modular filesystem
    plugins from Python</li>
</ul>

<h1>Release 2.3.1</h1>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>Fixes an undefined behavior causing a segfault in <code>tf.raw_ops.Switch</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15190">CVE-2020-15190</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes three vulnerabilities in conversion to DLPack format
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15191">CVE-2020-15191</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15192">CVE-2020-15192</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15193">CVE-2020-15193</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes two vulnerabilities in <code>SparseFillEmptyRowsGrad</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15194">CVE-2020-15194</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15195">CVE-2020-15195</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes several vulnerabilities in <code>RaggedCountSparseOutput</code> and
    <code>SparseCountSparseOutput</code> operations
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15196">CVE-2020-15196</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15197">CVE-2020-15197</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15198">CVE-2020-15198</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15199">CVE-2020-15199</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15200">CVE-2020-15200</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15201">CVE-2020-15201</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an integer truncation vulnerability in code using the work sharder API
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15202">CVE-2020-15202</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a format string vulnerability in <code>tf.strings.as_string</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15203">CVE-2020-15203</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes segfault raised by calling session-only ops in eager mode
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15204">CVE-2020-15204</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes data leak and potential ASLR violation from <code>tf.raw_ops.StringNGrams</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15205">CVE-2020-15205</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes segfaults caused by incomplete <code>SavedModel</code> validation
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15206">CVE-2020-15206</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a data corruption due to a bug in negative indexing support in TFLite
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15207">CVE-2020-15207</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a data corruption due to dimension mismatch in TFLite
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15208">CVE-2020-15208</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes several vulnerabilities in TFLite saved model format
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15209">CVE-2020-15209</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15210">CVE-2020-15210</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15211">CVE-2020-15211</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes several vulnerabilities in TFLite implementation of segment sum
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15212">CVE-2020-15212</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15213">CVE-2020-15213</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15214">CVE-2020-15214</a>)</li>
<li>Updates <code>sqlite3</code> to <code>3.33.00</code> to handle
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15358">CVE-2020-15358</a>.</li>
<li>Fixes deprecated usage of <code>collections</code> API</li>
<li>Removes <code>scipy</code> dependency from <code>setup.py</code> since TensorFlow does not need it
    to install the pip package</li>
</ul>

    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13630">CVE-2020-13630</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13631">CVE-2020-13631</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13871">CVE-2020-13871</a>,
    and
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15358">CVE-2020-15358</a>.</li>
<li>Pins <code>numpy</code> to 1.18.5 to prevent ABI breakage when compiling code that uses
    both NumPy and TensorFlow headers.</li>
</ul>
<h1>Release 1.15.4</h1>
<h2>Bug Fixes and Other Changes</h2>
<ul>
<li>Fixes an undefined behavior causing a segfault in <code>tf.raw_ops.Switch</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15190">CVE-2020-15190</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes three vulnerabilities in conversion to DLPack format
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15191">CVE-2020-15191</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15192">CVE-2020-15192</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15193">CVE-2020-15193</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes two vulnerabilities in <code>SparseFillEmptyRowsGrad</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15194">CVE-2020-15194</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15195">CVE-2020-15195</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes an integer truncation vulnerability in code using the work sharder API
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15202">CVE-2020-15202</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes a format string vulnerability in <code>tf.strings.as_string</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15203">CVE-2020-15203</a>)</li>

    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15204">CVE-2020-15204</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes data leak and potential ASLR violation from <code>tf.raw_ops.StringNGrams</code>
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15205">CVE-2020-15205</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes segfaults caused by incomplete <code>SavedModel</code> validation
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15206">CVE-2020-15206</a>)</li>

    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15207">CVE-2020-15207</a>)</li>

    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15208">CVE-2020-15208</a>)</li>
<li>Fixes several vulnerabilities in TFLite saved model format
    (<a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15209">CVE-2020-15209</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15210">CVE-2020-15210</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15211">CVE-2020-15211</a>)</li>
<li>Updates <code>sqlite3</code> to <code>3.33.00</code> to handle
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-9327">CVE-2020-9327</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-11655">CVE-2020-11655</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-11656">CVE-2020-11656</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13434">CVE-2020-13434</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13435">CVE-2020-13435</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13630">CVE-2020-13630</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13631">CVE-2020-13631</a>,
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-13871">CVE-2020-13871</a>,
    and
    <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2020-15358">CVE-2020-15358</a>.</li>
<li>Fixes #41630 by including <code>max_seq_length</code> in CuDNN descriptor cache key</li>
<li>Pins <code>numpy</code> to 1.18.5 to prevent ABI breakage when compiling code that uses
    both NumPy and TensorFlow headers.</li>
